PlanPrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
The available knowledge is insufficient to assess the Claim. Therefore, **propose a set of actions** to retrieve new and helpful evidence. Adhere to the following rules:
* The actions available are listed under Valid Actions, including a short description for each action. No other actions are possible at this moment. 
* For each action, use the formatting as specified in Valid Actions.
* Include all actions in a single Markdown code block at the end of your answer.
* Propose as few actions as possible, but as much as needed. Do not propose similar or previously used actions.



## Valid Actions
* `reverse_search`
   * Description: Performs a reverse image search to find similar images on the web.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will perform a reverse search to find similar images.
   * Format: reverse_search(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `image_search`
   * Description: Run an image search on Google to retrieve related images for a given query.
   * How to use: This is a helpful tool for fact-checking images. Use this to retrieve images associated with a specific keyword or phrase. Ensure that the query is clear and specific to improve search accuracy. If no relevant images are found, refine the query or use more descriptive terms.
   * Format: image_search("your image search query goes here")

* `geolocate`
   * Description: Performs geolocation to determine the country where an image was taken.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will determine the most likely countries where it was taken.
   * Format: geolocate(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `web_search`
   * Description: Run an open web search on Google or DuckDuckGO to retrieve any related webpage.
   * How to use: Do not use this with a previously used or similar query from previous web searches. If a previous web search did not yield any results, use a very different query.
   * Format: web_search("your web search query goes here")

# Example: reverse_search()

## Claim
Text: "<image:k> shows a rare event of a solar eclipse with a double ring."

...

## Actions
```
reverse_search(<image:k>)
```

# Example: image_search()

## Claim
Text: "Chinese officials in white protective hazmat suits carried people down a hallway to be quarantined for having COVID-19 in November 2022."

...

ACTIONS:
```
image_search("China officials white suits carry people")
image_search("China officials carry people COVID quarantine 2022")
```

# Example: geolocate()

## Claim
Text: "<image:k> shows a nuclear weapons facility in Usbekistan."

...

## Actions
```
geolocate(<image:k>)
```

# Example: web_search()

## Claim
Text: "New Zealand’s new Food Bill bans gardening"
Claim date: October 29, 2020

...

## Actions
```
web_search("New Zealand Food Bill 2020")
web_search("New Zealand Food Bill gardening ban")
```

# Record
## Claim
Claim: "China and Japan plan to invade the Russian Federation."

# Your Actions



===== > RESPONSE:  < =====
```
web_search("China Japan invade Russia")
```
_________________________



SummarizeResultPrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
In order to find evidence that helps your fact-check, you just ran a web search which yielded a Search Result. **Your task right now is to summarize the Search Result.** What to include:
* information that might be useful for the fact-check (see Record)
* relevant images (refer to images by inserting their reference <image:k>)
* if available: the release date as well as the author or the publisher (e.g. the media company) of the search result.

Do NOT include:
* advertisements
* any other information not related to the Record or the Claim

Additional rules:
* Do not add any additional information besides the information in the Search Result.
* If the Search Result doesn't contain any relevant information for the fact-checking work, simply print one word in capital letters: "NONE".
* Keep your writing style like in the Examples 1, 2 and 3 provided to you.
* Try to filter out relevant information even if the search result is in a different language.

# Example 1
The search result from America Today provides several photographs of the Notre-Dame Cathedral fire on April 15, 2019. <image:i>, <image:j>, <image:k>. None of the images show the Eiffel Tower in the background. 

# Example 2
NONE

# Example 3
The Guardian discusses a report blaming the Syrian government for a toxic gas attack and condemning their use of chemical weapons. The Guardian mentions the Chemical Weapons Convention and the responsibilities of Syria under the convention. According to The Guardian, The White House condemned the Assad regime for defying the norm against chemical weapons use.

# Record
## Claim
Claim: "China and Japan plan to invade the Russian Federation."

## Actions
```
web_search("China Japan invade Russia")
```

Soviet invasion of Manchuria

[](#)
[](#)
[](#)
[](#)
[](#)
[](#)
[](#)

39 languages [Add topic](#) By early 1945 it had become apparent to the Japanese that the Soviets were preparing to invade Manchuria, though they correctly calculated that they were unlikely to attack prior to Germany's defeat. For the 1900 Russian invasion, see [Russian invasion of Manchuria](/wiki/Russian_invasion_of_Manchuria "Russian invasion of Manchuria")
.

Soviet invasion of ManchuriaPart of the [Soviet–Japanese War](/wiki/Soviet%E2%80%93Japanese_War "Soviet–Japanese War")
 of [World War II](/wiki/World_War_II "World War II")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Manchuria_Operation_map-en.svg/330px-Manchuria_Operation_map-en.svg.png)](/wiki/File:Manchuria_Operation_map-en.svg)
  
Soviet gains in North East Asia, August 1945

|     |     |
| --- | --- |
| Date | 9–20 August 1945 |
| Location | [Manchuria](/wiki/Manchuria "Manchuria")<br>, [Inner Mongolia](/wiki/Inner_Mongolia "Inner Mongolia")<br>, and northern [Korea](/wiki/Korea "Korea") |
| Result | Soviet victory |
| Territorial  <br>changes | Collapse of Japanese puppet states<br><br>*   Partition of the Korean Peninsula at the [38th parallel](/wiki/Division_of_Korea "Division of Korea")<br>    .<br>*   Most of Manchuria and Inner Mongolia are returned to [the Nationalist government of China](/wiki/Nationalist_government "Nationalist government")<br>     by a 1945 [bilateral agreement](/wiki/Sino-Soviet_Treaty_of_Friendship_and_Alliance "Sino-Soviet Treaty of Friendship and Alliance")<br>    <br>*   Parts of [Manchuria](/wiki/Manchuria "Manchuria")<br>     and [Inner Mongolia](/wiki/Inner_Mongolia "Inner Mongolia")<br>     are secretly handed over to the [Chinese Communist Party](/wiki/Chinese_Communist_Party "Chinese Communist Party")<br>     [guerrillas](/wiki/Guerrilla "Guerrilla")<br>     after the Soviet withdrawal in 1946 |

Strength

[![Soviet Union](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union_%281936_%E2%80%93_1955%29.svg/40px-Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union_%281936_%E2%80%93_1955%29.svg.png)](/wiki/Soviet_Union "Soviet Union")
 **Soviet Union:**

*   1,577,725 troops[\[3\]](#cite_note-glantz378-3)
    
*   27,086 artillery pieces
*   1,152 rocket launchers
*   5,556 tanks and self-propelled guns
*   3,721 aircraft
*   [![Mongolian People's Republic](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Flag_of_the_Mongolian_People%27s_Republic_%281945%E2%80%931992%29.svg/40px-Flag_of_the_Mongolian_People%27s_Republic_%281945%E2%80%931992%29.svg.png)](/wiki/Mongolian_People%27s_Republic "Mongolian People's Republic")
     **Mongolia:**
*   16,000 troops

* * *

*   **Total:**
*   1,593,725 troops
*   27,086 artillery pieces
*   1,152 rocket launchers
*   5,556 tanks and self-propelled guns
*   3,721 aircraft

[![Empire of Japan](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Flag_of_Japan_%281870%E2%80%931999%29.svg/40px-Flag_of_Japan_%281870%E2%80%931999%29.svg.png)](/wiki/Empire_of_Japan "Empire of Japan")
 **Japan:**

*   _Manchuria:_
*   665,500 soldiers and sailors[\[4\]](#cite_note-:1-4)
    [\[a\]](#cite_note-6)
    
*   290 tanks[\[6\]](#cite_note-7)
    
*   1,042 aircraft (232 combat)[\[7\]](#cite_note-:2-8)
    [\[b\]](#cite_note-9)
    
*   _Korea:_
*   335,900 soldiers and sailors[\[4\]](#cite_note-:1-4)
      
    ~80 tanks[\[c\]](#cite_note-10)
    
*   962 aircraft (395 combat)[\[7\]](#cite_note-:2-8)
    
*   [![Manchukuo](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Flag_of_Manchukuo.svg/40px-Flag_of_Manchukuo.svg.png)](/wiki/Manchukuo "Manchukuo")
     **Manchukuo:**
*   170,000[\[1\]](#cite_note-Glantz-1)
    –200,000 troops[\[8\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJowett53-11)
    
*   [![Mengjiang](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Flag_of_the_Mengjiang.svg/40px-Flag_of_the_Mengjiang.svg.png)](/wiki/Mengjiang "Mengjiang")
     **Mengjiang:**
*   44,000 troops

* * *

*   **Total:**
*   1,215,400–1,245,400 troops and sailor
*   370 tanks
*   2,004 aircraft (627 combat)

Casualties and losses

[![Soviet Union](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union_%281936_%E2%80%93_1955%29.svg/40px-Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union_%281936_%E2%80%93_1955%29.svg.png)](/wiki/Soviet_Union "Soviet Union")
 **Soviet Union:**

*   9,780–12,031 killed
*   24,425 wounded[\[9\]](#cite_note-12)
    [\[10\]](#cite_note-Coox,_Alvin_D._1939-13)
    
*   300+ tanks destroyed[\[11\]](#cite_note-14)

The **Soviet invasion of Manchuria**, formally known as the **Manchurian Strategic Offensive Operation**[\[15\]](#cite_note-22)
 or simply the **Manchurian Operation** (Маньчжурская операция) and sometimes **Operation August Storm**,[\[1\]](#cite_note-Glantz-1)
 began on 9 August 1945 with the [Soviet](/wiki/Soviet_Union "Soviet Union")
 invasion of the [Empire of Japan](/wiki/Empire_of_Japan "Empire of Japan")
's [puppet state](/wiki/Puppet_state "Puppet state")
 of [Manchukuo](/wiki/Manchukuo "Manchukuo")
, which was situated in Japanese-occupied [Manchuria](/wiki/Manchuria "Manchuria")
. Soviet paratroopers destroyed the Kwantung Army from behind its own lines, while Japanese anti-tank shells bounced off the sides of Soviet tanks.[\[39\]](#cite_note-47)
 The Japanese forces in Manchuria retreated in fear.[\[40\]](#cite_note-48)

Japanese troops and able-bodied Japanese men in Manchuria were taken prisoner by the Russians and transported to labor camps in Siberia, where many Japanese men would die.[\[41\]](#cite_note-49)
 From the Russians' perspective, this was seen as revenge for Russia's defeat in the [Russo-Japanese War](/wiki/Russo-Japanese_War "Russo-Japanese War")
 of 1905.[\[42\]](#cite_note-50)
 The stories of how poorly the Soviets treated the Japanese were brought to [Beijing](/wiki/Beijing "Beijing")
 by Japanese evacuees of Manchuria, creating panic among the Japanese population; however, the Russians honored their agreement with Chiang Kai-shek by not entering China proper.[\[43\]](#cite_note-51)

Japanese communication infrastructure was poor, and the Japanese lost communication with forward units very early on. reports indicate that the Soviet troops that occupied Manchuria (about 700,000) also looted and terrorized the local people of Mukden and were not discouraged by Soviet authorities from "three days of rape and pillage." In Harbin, Soviet forces ignored protests from [Chinese Communist Party](/wiki/Communist_Party_of_China "Communist Party of China")
 leaders on the mass rape and looting.[\[62\]](#cite_note-FCJones-70)
[\[63\]](#cite_note-CSM-71)
[\[64\]](#cite_note-72)
[\[65\]](#cite_note-73)
[\[66\]](#cite_note-74)
[\[67\]](#cite_note-75)
 There were several incidents in which Chinese police forces in Manchuria arrested or even killed Soviet troops for committing various crimes, leading to some conflicts between the Soviet and Chinese authorities in Manchuria.[\[68\]](#cite_note-76)

During the [Soviet occupation of North Korea](/wiki/Soviet_Civil_Administration "Soviet Civil Administration")
, it was reported that Soviet soldiers committed rape against both [Japanese](/wiki/Japanese_people "Japanese people")
 and [Korean](/wiki/Koreans "Koreans")
 women alike in the northern half of the Korean peninsula.[\[69\]](#cite_note-77)
[\[70\]](#cite_note-78)
 Soviet soldiers also looted the property of both Japanese and Koreans living in northern Korea.[\[71\]](#cite_note-:0-79)
 The Soviets laid claim to Japanese enterprises in Manchuria and northern Korea and took valuable materials and industrial equipment.[\[62\]](#cite_note-FCJones-70)
[\[71\]](#cite_note-:0-79)

Konstantin Asmolov of the Center for Korean Research of the [Russian Academy of Sciences](/wiki/Russian_Academy_of_Sciences "Russian Academy of Sciences")
 dismisses Western accounts of Soviet violence against civilians in the Far East as exaggeration and rumor and contends that accusations of mass crimes by the Red Army inappropriately extrapolate isolated incidents regarding the nearly 2,000,000 Soviet troops in the Far East into mass crimes. **[^](#cite_ref-CSM_71-0)
    ** _Christian Science Monitor_, 12 October 1945, Japanese armies were guilty of appalling excesses, both in China and elsewhere, and had the Russians dealt harshly with only Japanese nationals in Manchuria this would have appeared as just retribution. The Japanese did not have any concrete evidence as to when or where any invasion would occur.[\[17\]](#cite_note-Drea-24)
 They had estimated that an attack was not likely before the spring of 1946, but the _[Stavka](/wiki/Stavka "Stavka")
_ had in fact been planning for a mid-August offensive, successfully [concealing the buildup](/wiki/Russian_military_deception "Russian military deception")
 of a force of 90 divisions. This attack involved the [1st Red Banner Army](/wiki/Soviet_First_Army "Soviet First Army")
, the [5th Army](/wiki/5th_Army_(Soviet_Union) "5th Army (Soviet Union)")
 and the [10th Mechanized Corps](/wiki/10th_Mechanized_Corps "10th Mechanized Corps")
 striking towards [Mudanjiang](/wiki/Mudanjiang "Mudanjiang")
 (or Mutanchiang).[\[1\]](#cite_note-Glantz-1)
 Once that city was captured, this force was to advance towards the cities of [Jilin](/wiki/Jilin "Jilin")
 (or Kirin), Changchun and Harbin.[\[1\]](#cite_note-Glantz-1)
 Its final objective was to link up with the forces of the Transbaikal Front at Changchun and Jilin thus closing the double envelopment movement.

As a secondary objective, the 1st Far Eastern Front was to prevent Japanese forces from escaping to [Korea](/wiki/Korea "Korea")
, and then invade the [Korean Peninsula](/wiki/Korean_Peninsula "Korean Peninsula")
 up to the [38th parallel](/wiki/38th_parallel_north#Korea "38th parallel north")
,[\[1\]](#cite_note-Glantz-1)
 establishing in the process what later became [North Korea](/wiki/North_Korea "North Korea")
. This secondary objective was to be carried out by the [25th Army](/wiki/25th_Army_(Soviet_Union) "25th Army (Soviet Union)")
.[\[1\]](#cite_note-Glantz-1)
 Meanwhile, the [35th Army](/wiki/35th_Army_(Russia) "35th Army (Russia)")
 was tasked with capturing the cities of [Boli](/wiki/Boli_County "Boli County")
 (or Poli), [Linkou](/w/index.php?title=Linkou,_Heilongjiang&action=edit&redlink=1 "Linkou, Heilongjiang (page does not exist)")
 and [Mishan](/wiki/Mishan "Mishan")
.[\[1\]](#cite_note-Glantz-1)

#### 2nd Far Eastern Front

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Soviet_invasion_of_Manchuria&action=edit&section=7 "Edit section: 2nd Far Eastern Front")\
\]

The 2nd Far Eastern Front, under General [Maksim Purkayev](/wiki/Maksim_Purkayev "Maksim Purkayev")
, included:[\[1\]](#cite_note-Glantz-1)

*   [2nd Red Banner Army](/wiki/Soviet_Second_Army "Soviet Second Army")
    
*   [15th Army](/wiki/15th_Army_(Soviet_Union) "15th Army (Soviet Union)")
    
*   [16th Army](/wiki/16th_Army_(Soviet_Union) "16th Army (Soviet Union)")
     (whose 56th Rifle Corps was its only formation to see combat, on [South Sakhalin](/wiki/South_Sakhalin "South Sakhalin")
    )
*   [5th Separate Rifle Corps](/wiki/5th_Separate_Rifle_Corps "5th Separate Rifle Corps")
    
*   [Chuguevsk Operational Group](/w/index.php?title=Chuguevsk_Operational_Group&action=edit&redlink=1 "Chuguevsk Operational Group (page does not exist)")
    
*   [Amur Military Flotilla](/wiki/Amur_Military_Flotilla "Amur Military Flotilla")
    
*   [10th Air Army](/wiki/10th_Air_Army "10th Air Army")
    

The 2nd Far Eastern Front was deployed in a supporting attack role.[\[1\]](#cite_note-Glantz-1)
 Its objectives were the cities of Harbin and Qiqihar,[\[2\]](#cite_note-Battlefield_Series-2)
 and to prevent an orderly withdrawal to the south by the Japanese forces.[\[1\]](#cite_note-Glantz-1)
 The front also included the [88th Separate Rifle Brigade](/wiki/88th_Separate_Rifle_Brigade "88th Separate Rifle Brigade")
, composed of Chinese and Korean guerrillas of the [Northeast Anti-Japanese United Army](/wiki/Northeast_Anti-Japanese_United_Army "Northeast Anti-Japanese United Army")
 who had retreated into the USSR in the beginning of the 1940s. The Kwantung Army commanders were engaged in a planning exercise at the time of the invasion, and were away from their forces for the first eighteen hours of conflict.

The Russians treated the Japanese with the utmost cruelty after their deadly attack on Japan's Kwantung Army in Manchuria just days before Japan's surrender.[\[38\]](#cite_note-46)
 Japanese forces were overwhelmed by Soviet attacks."

# Your Summary



===== > RESPONSE:  < =====
The Soviet Union invaded Manchuria in August 1945, defeating the Japanese Kwantung Army. The invasion resulted in the collapse of Japanese puppet states, the partition of the Korean Peninsula, and the return of most of Manchuria and Inner Mongolia to the Nationalist government of China. The search result also mentions the involvement of Mongolia in the invasion. The Japanese forces were taken prisoner and transported to labor camps in Siberia. The result also mentions looting and violence against civilians by Soviet troops.

By: HISTORY.com Editors

1945

Soviets declare war on Japan, invade Manchuria the next day
===========================================================

[HISTORY.com Editors](/authors/history)

Published: August 06, 2010

Last Updated: May 27, 2025

Print

Share

On August 8, 1945, the [Soviet Union](/topics/history-of-the-soviet-union)
 officially [declares war on Japan](https://blog.nationalarchives.gov.uk/soviet-japan-and-the-termination-of-the-second-world-war/#:~:text=However%2C%20on%208,Japan%20to%20surrender.)
, pouring more than 1 million Soviet soldiers the following day into [Japanese-occupied Manchuria](https://blog.nationalarchives.gov.uk/soviet-japan-and-the-termination-of-the-second-world-war/#:~:text=The%20Soviets%20launched%20their%20invasion%20simultaneously%20on%20three%20fronts%20in%20the%20east%2C%20west%20and%20north%20of%20Manchuria%2C%20the%20day%20after%20the%20declaration%20of%20war.)
, northeastern China, to take on the 700,000-strong Japanese army.

The [dropping of the bomb on Hiroshima](https://www.history.com/topics/world-war-ii/bombing-of-hiroshima-and-nagasaki)
 by the Americans did not have the effect intended: unconditional surrender by Japan. But if you see something that doesn't look right, [click here](mailto:support@history.zendesk.com?subject=Fact%20Check%20-%20Soviets%20declare%20war%20on%20Japan%2C%20invade%20Manchuria%20the%20next%20day)
 to contact us! HISTORY reviews and updates its content regularly to ensure it is complete and accurate.

Uncover fascinating moments from the past every day! Half of the Japanese inner Cabinet, called the Supreme War Direction Council, refused to surrender unless guarantees about Japan’s future were given by the Allies, especially regarding the position of the emperor, [Hirohito](/topics/world-war-ii/hirohito)
. The only Japanese civilians who even knew what happened at Hiroshima were either dead or suffering terribly.

Japan had not been too worried about the Soviet Union, so busy with the Germans on the Eastern front. The Japanese army went so far as to believe that they would not have to engage a Soviet attack until spring 1946. But the Soviets surprised them one day after the declaration of war with their invasion of Manchuria, an assault so strong (of the 850 Japanese soldiers engaged at Pingyanchen, 650 were killed or wounded within the first two days of fighting) that Emperor Hirohito began to plead with his War Council to reconsider surrender. Top Questions

### 

What caused the Russo-Japanese War?

The war developed from [Russia](https://www.britannica.com/place/Russia)
’s and [Japan](https://www.britannica.com/place/Japan)
’s rivalry for dominance in [Korea](https://www.britannica.com/place/Korea)
 and [Manchuria](https://www.britannica.com/place/Manchuria)
. The engagement took place on May 27–29, 1905, with Japan inflicting a crushing defeat on the Russian navy.(more)

**Russo-Japanese War**, (1904–05), military conflict in which a victorious [Japan](https://www.britannica.com/place/Japan)
 forced [Russia](https://www.britannica.com/place/Russia)
 to abandon its expansionist policy in [East Asia](https://www.britannica.com/place/East-Asia)
, thereby becoming the first Asian power in modern times to defeat a European power.

Origins of the Russo-Japanese War
---------------------------------

[![Russian Empire](https://cdn.britannica.com/50/3850-050-460382BE/Russian-expansion-Asia.jpg?w=300)](https://cdn.britannica.com/50/3850-050-460382BE/Russian-expansion-Asia.jpg)

Russian Empire <image:2464>
Map of Russian expansion in Asia, 1533–1894.(more)

By the early 17th century, Russia had established its authority over all of [Siberia](https://www.britannica.com/place/Siberia)
, but its attempts to move southward were consistently blocked by [China](https://www.britannica.com/place/China)
. Japan, with its modernized army and navy, at once won a series of striking victories against the Chinese, who, in the [Treaty of Shimonoseki](https://www.britannica.com/event/Treaty-of-Shimonoseki)
 (April 17, 1895), ceded to Japan the [Kwantung (Liaodong) Peninsula](https://www.britannica.com/place/Liaodong-Peninsula)
, on which Port Arthur (now [Dalian](https://www.britannica.com/place/Dalian)
) stands, together with Formosa ([Taiwan](https://www.britannica.com/place/Taiwan)
) and the [Pescadores (P’eng-hu) Islands](https://www.britannica.com/place/Peng-hu-Islands)
, and agreed to pay a heavy indemnity.

This display of Japanese power and its decisive victory over China threatened to close the door on Russia in East Asia, and it made conflict between Russia and Japan inevitable. In 1896 Russia concluded an alliance with China against Japan, guaranteeing the [integrity](https://www.merriam-webster.com/dictionary/integrity)
 of Chinese territory. Russia thus entered into the occupation of the Kwantung Peninsula, from which only three years earlier it had excluded Japan.

[![What happened during the Boxer Rebellion in China?](https://cdn.britannica.com/15/180115-138-76A93B98/Video-overview-Boxer-Rebellion.jpg?w=800&h=450&c=crop)](/video/Video-overview-Boxer-Rebellion/-203056)

What happened during the Boxer Rebellion in China?Video overview of the Boxer Rebellion.(more)

[See all videos for this article](/event/Russo-Japanese-War/images-videos)

The seizure of Chinese territory by Germany and Russia was followed by British demands for [Weihai](https://www.britannica.com/place/Weihai)
 and French claims on Kwangchow (now [Guangzhou](https://www.britannica.com/place/Guangzhou)
). Realizing that Japan had gained preponderance in East Asia, in the summer of 1903 he recommended that Russia should abandon its projects in Manchuria and restore Port Arthur to China in return for [concessions](https://www.merriam-webster.com/dictionary/concessions)
 in the Vladivostok region. However, the lessons of Port Arthur would go largely unheeded by European commanders, who would replicate the same sanguinary tactics on the [Western Front](https://www.britannica.com/event/Western-Front-World-War-I)
 during [World War I](https://www.britannica.com/event/World-War-I)
.

[![Russo-Japanese War](https://cdn.britannica.com/07/146507-050-F4C5DF77/Meeting-Russian-generals-terms-Japanese-surrender-Russo-Japanese.jpg?w=300)\
\
1 of 3](https://cdn.britannica.com/07/146507-050-F4C5DF77/Meeting-Russian-generals-terms-Japanese-surrender-Russo-Japanese.jpg)

[Russo-Japanese War](https://cdn.britannica.com/07/146507-050-F4C5DF77/Meeting-Russian-generals-terms-Japanese-surrender-Russo-Japanese.jpg)
Meeting between Anatoly Stessel of Russia and Nogi Maresuke of Japan, opposing generals in the Russo-Japanese War, January 27, 1905.(more)

[![Russo-Japanese War](https://cdn.britannica.com/06/146506-050-1B0D0997/Anatoly-Stessel-Russia-toast-generals-Japan-Nogi-Jan-27-1905.jpg?w=300)\
\
2 of 3](https://cdn.britannica.com/06/146506-050-1B0D0997/Anatoly-Stessel-Russia-toast-generals-Japan-Nogi-Jan-27-1905.jpg)

[Russo-Japanese War](https://cdn.britannica.com/06/146506-050-1B0D0997/Anatoly-Stessel-Russia-toast-generals-Japan-Nogi-Jan-27-1905.jpg)
Anatoly Stessel (left) of Russia and Nogi Maresuke of Japan, opposing generals in the Russo-Japanese War, sharing a toast after arranging the terms of Russia's surrender of Port Arthur (now Lüshun, China), January 27, 1905.(more)

[![Battleships at Port Arthur](https://cdn.britannica.com/14/146514-050-E3227B03/battleships-Russian-Port-Arthur-Russo-Japanese-War-1904.jpg?w=300)\
\
3 of 3](https://cdn.britannica.com/14/146514-050-E3227B03/battleships-Russian-Port-Arthur-Russo-Japanese-War-1904.jpg)

[Battleships at Port Arthur](https://cdn.britannica.com/14/146514-050-E3227B03/battleships-Russian-Port-Arthur-Russo-Japanese-War-1904.jpg)
Stranded Russian battleships at Port Arthur days before its fall during the Russo-Japanese War, 1904.(more)

Among the Russian commanders at Port Arthur there was serious disagreement. Russia agreed to evacuate southern Manchuria, which was restored to China, and Japan’s control of Korea was recognized. Russia nevertheless remained an Asian power, possessing as it did the railways across Siberia and northern Manchuria to Vladivostok and being closely allied with China.

Japan, for its part, formalized its hold on Korea by forcing [Kojong](https://www.britannica.com/biography/Gojong)
, the final monarch of the Chosŏn (Yi) [dynasty](https://www.merriam-webster.com/dictionary/dynasty)
, to [abdicate](https://www.merriam-webster.com/dictionary/abdicate)
 in 1907."

The war's origins are rooted in the rivalry between Russia and Japan for dominance in Korea and Manchuria. <image:2464> shows the Russian expansion in Asia. The article also mentions the Treaty of Shimonoseki, where Japan gained control of the Kwantung Peninsula.

Content: The Soviet Union invaded Manchuria in August 1945, defeating the Japanese Kwantung Army. The invasion resulted in the collapse of Japanese puppet states, the partition of the Korean Peninsula, and the return of most of Manchuria and Inner Mongolia to the Nationalist government of China. The search result also mentions the involvement of Mongolia in the invasion. The Japanese forces were taken prisoner and transported to labor camps in Siberia. The result also mentions looting and violence against civilians by Soviet troops.

The war's origins are rooted in the rivalry between Russia and Japan for dominance in Korea and Manchuria. <image:2464> shows the Russian expansion in Asia. The Soviet Union invaded Manchuria in August 1945, defeating the Japanese Kwantung Army, which led to the collapse of Japanese puppet states and the return of Manchuria and Inner Mongolia to China. ([https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_invasion_of_Manchuria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_invasion_of_Manchuria)) History.com published an article discussing the Soviet Union's declaration of war on Japan on August 8, 1945, and the subsequent invasion of Manchuria the following day <image:i>. The Russo-Japanese War (1904-1905) between Japan and Russia, fought over dominance in Korea and Manchuria, resulted in Japan's victory, becoming the first Asian power to defeat a European power. <image:2464> ([https://www.britannica.com/event/Russo-Japanese-War](https://www.britannica.com/event/Russo-Japanese-War))

# Instructions
**Determine the Claim's veracity** by following these steps:
1. Briefly summarize the key insights from the fact-check (see Record) in at most one paragraph.
2. Write one paragraph about which one of the Decision Options applies best. Include the most appropriate decision option at the end and enclose it in backticks like `this`.



## Decision Options
* `false`: The claim is not factually accurate. This is the case if one of the following three conditions is met:(1) The claim is demonstrably false when it is disproven by evidence from multiple and reliable sources,(2) The claim or image is taken out of context, i.e. the origin, content and/or meaning of a statement or an image is misrepresented. For example, an old claim or an old image is mispresented in a new context in a misleading way,(3) There is not enough evidence to verify the claim or the evidence is conflicting or self-contradictory.
* `not enough information`: The fact-check does not contain sufficient information to come to an conclusion. For example,there is substantial lack of evidence or the evidence is inconclusive, conflicting or self-contradictory. In the case of a lack of evidence, state which information exactly is missing. In particular, if no RESULTS or sources are available, pick this decision.
* `true`: The claim is factually accurate when it is confirmed by evidence from multiple and reliable sources.

The Russo-Japanese War (1904-1905) between Japan and Russia, fought over dominance in Korea and Manchuria, resulted in Japan's victory, becoming the first Asian power to defeat a European power. <image:2464> ([https://www.britannica.com/event/Russo-Japanese-War](https://www.britannica.com/event/Russo-Japanese-War))

# Instructions
The available knowledge is insufficient to assess the Claim. Therefore, **propose a set of actions** to retrieve new and helpful evidence. Adhere to the following rules:
* The actions available are listed under Valid Actions, including a short description for each action. No other actions are possible at this moment. 
* For each action, use the formatting as specified in Valid Actions.
* Include all actions in a single Markdown code block at the end of your answer.
* Propose as few actions as possible, but as much as needed. Do not propose similar or previously used actions.



## Valid Actions
* `reverse_search`
   * Description: Performs a reverse image search to find similar images on the web.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will perform a reverse search to find similar images.
   * Format: reverse_search(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `image_search`
   * Description: Run an image search on Google to retrieve related images for a given query.
   * How to use: This is a helpful tool for fact-checking images. Use this to retrieve images associated with a specific keyword or phrase. Ensure that the query is clear and specific to improve search accuracy. If no relevant images are found, refine the query or use more descriptive terms.
   * Format: image_search("your image search query goes here")

* `geolocate`
   * Description: Performs geolocation to determine the country where an image was taken.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will determine the most likely countries where it was taken.
   * Format: geolocate(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `web_search`
   * Description: Run an open web search on Google or DuckDuckGO to retrieve any related webpage.
   * How to use: Do not use this with a previously used or similar query from previous web searches. If a previous web search did not yield any results, use a very different query.
   * Format: web_search("your web search query goes here")

Russia, China Simulate Attack on Enemy Submarine in Sea of Japan Drills
=======================================================================

[Dzirhan Mahadzir](https://news.usni.org/author/dmahadzir)

August 6, 2025 3:43 PM

![](https://news.usni.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/Screenshot-2025-08-06-at-3.10.05 PM.png)

Russia and China wrapped up their joint exercise – dubbed Maritime Interaction 2025 by Russia and Joint Sea 2025 by China – Aug. Image via PLAN media

The Russian Navy and People’s Liberation Army Navy (PLAN) simulated attacks on an adversarial submarine and an amphibious ship, and rehearsed a submarine rescue during a recent five-day joint exercise in the Sea of Japan.

A Russian Navy IL-38 and PLAN Y-8 maritime patrol aircraft located and destroyed a simulated enemy submarine in a joint anti-submarine warfare drill in the Sea of Japan, the Russian Ministry of Defense said Wednesday. The two countries also conducted joint firing exercises, using naval guns to fire at a naval target meant to imitate an enemy assault landing ship detachment.

Russia and China wrapped up their joint exercise – dubbed [Maritime Interaction 2025 by Russia and Joint Sea 2025 by China](https://news.usni.org/2025/08/01/chinese-submarine-makes-first-visit-to-russia-for-joint-drills)
 – on Tuesday following several days of drills. The crew of _Volkhov_ simulated evacuating personnel from the submarine.

Following the completion of the drill between _Volkhov_ and _Xihu_, _Igor Belousov_ carried out a similar exercise with the PLAN submarine, according to the release.

“Russian rescue sailors shared their experience with their Chinese colleagues, demonstrating the capabilities of modern medical equipment, pressure chambers and an AS-40 deep-sea rescue submersible vehicle,” the Russian Ministry of Defense said.

CNS _Shaoxing_ and _Qiandaohu_ carried out a separate set of activities in the Sea of Japan. In both cases, fleet oiler JS _Towada_ (AOE-422) and a Japan Maritime Self-Defense Force P-3C Orion MPA shadowed the PLAN ships, according to the JSO release.

Three Russian ships – including a Udaloy-class destroyer, a Ropucha-class tank landing ship, and a Steregushchiy-class frigate – were sighted Saturday sailing east approximately 43 miles northwest of Rebun Island, which lies 31 miles west of Japan’s main island of Hokkaido.

The ships transited east through La Pérouse Strait, which separates Hokkaido from Russia’s Sakhalin Island, to enter the Sea of Okhotsk. La Pérouse Strait is an international waterway and a regular transit route for Russian Navy ships moving between the Sea of Japan and the Sea of Okhotsk.

JMSDF fast attack craft JS _Wakataka_ (PG-825) conducted surveillance on the Russian ships, according to the JSO release.

The three Russian ships are likely part of the Russian Pacific fleet detachment, which includes destroyer RFS _Admiral Panteleyev_ (548), corvette RFS _Sovershennyy_, amphibious landing ship RFS _Oslyabya_ (066), submarine RFS _Magadan_ (B-602) and rescue tug _Alatau_.

The Russian Pacific fleet is conducting a patriotic and information deployment campaign called “Strength in Truth-2025.” As part of the campaign, the four ships and a submarine are expected to sail to various ports in the Russian Far East to commemorate Russia’s role in World War II, and the activities of Russian Pacific Fleet personnel in the Ukraine conflict.

_Admiral Panteleyev, Sovershennyy, Oslyabya_ and _Magadan_ left Vladivostok on Monday for the deployment. <image:2528>](https://news.usni.org/2025/08/05/army-deploys-hypersonic-missiles-to-indo-pacific-for-australian-drills)

Content: "![Chinese and Russian naval vessels are seen.](/wp-content/uploads/2019/06/a0ecaf8c581f41059664f9d52c89e8b0_18.jpeg?resize=770%2C513&quality=80)

Chinese and Russian naval vessels \[File: China Daily/Handout via Reuters\]

Published On 3 Aug 20253 Aug 2025

China and Russia have begun joint naval drills in the Sea of Japan as they seek to reinforce their partnership and counterbalance what they see as a United States-led global order.

The Chinese and Russian governments have [deepened](/video/newsfeed/2025/5/8/president-xi-china-and-russia-should-safeguard-international-justice)
 their ties in recent years, with China providing an economic lifeline to Russia in the face of Western sanctions over Moscow’s invasion of Ukraine.

end of list

The Joint Sea-2025 exercises began in waters near the Russian port of Vladivostok and will last for three days, China’s Ministry of National Defence said in a statement on Sunday.

The two sides will hold “submarine rescue, joint anti-submarine, air defence and anti-missile operations, and maritime combat”.

Four Chinese vessels, including guided-missile destroyers Shaoxing and Urumqi, are participating in the exercises, alongside Russian ships, the ministry said.

After the drills, the two countries will conduct naval patrols in “relevant waters of the Pacific”.

![Putin Xi](/wp-content/uploads/2025/03/GettyImages-1139368231-1741886998.jpg?w=770&resize=770%2C513&quality=80)

Russian President Vladimir Putin, left, shakes hands with Chinese President Xi Jinping \[File: Kenzaburo Fukuhara/Handout via Getty Images\]

China and Russia have carried out annual drills for several years, with the “Joint Sea” exercises beginning in 2012.

Last year’s drills were held along China’s southern coast.

With this year’s drills in the Sea of Japan, in its annual report last month, Japan’s Ministry of Defence warned that China’s growing military cooperation with Russia poses serious security concerns.

“The exercise is defensive in nature and is not directed against other countries,” the Russian Navy Pacific Fleet said earlier this week, according to a report by the US Naval Institute’s online news and analysis portal.

On Friday, the Chinese Defence Ministry said this year’s exercises were aimed at “further deepening the comprehensive strategic partnership” of the two countries.

China has never denounced Russia’s more than three-year [war](/video/newsfeed/2025/8/3/ukraine-claims-drone-strike-on-oil-refinery-in-russia)
 nor called for it to withdraw its troops, and many of Ukraine’s allies, including the US, believe that Beijing has provided support to Moscow.

European leaders asked China last month to use its influence to pressure Russia to end the war, now in its fourth year, but there was no sign that Beijing would do so.

China, however, insists it is a neutral party, regularly calling for an end to the fighting while also accusing Western countries of prolonging the conflict by arming Ukraine.

Source: News Agencies

aj-logo

aj-logo"

# Your Summary



===== > RESPONSE:  < =====
Al Jazeera published an article on August 3, 2025, reporting on joint naval drills between China and Russia in the Sea of Japan. <image:i>, <image:2464>. The exercises, which have been held annually since 2012, involve submarine rescue, anti-submarine, air defense, and anti-missile operations. Japan's Ministry of Defence has expressed security concerns about the growing military cooperation between China and Russia.

* relevant images (refer to images by inserting their reference <image:k>)

Do NOT include:
* advertisements

# Record
## Claim
Claim: "China and Japan plan to invade the Russian Federation."

## Actions
```
web_search("China Japan invade Russia")
```

## Evidence
### Evidence from `web_search`
The Soviet Union invaded Manchuria in August 1945, defeating the Japanese Kwantung Army, which led to the collapse of Japanese puppet states and the return of Manchuria and Inner Mongolia to China. The invasion also involved Mongolia and resulted in the capture of Japanese forces and looting by Soviet troops. ([https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_invasion_of_Manchuria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_invasion_of_Manchuria)) History.com published an article discussing the Soviet Union's declaration of war on Japan on August 8, 1945, and the subsequent invasion of Manchuria the following day <image:i>. ([https://www.history.com/this-day-in-history/august-8/soviets-declare-war-on-japan-invade-manchuria](https://www.history.com/this-day-in-history/august-8/soviets-declare-war-on-japan-invade-manchuria))

The Russo-Japanese War (1904-1905) between Japan and Russia, fought over dominance in Korea and Manchuria, resulted in Japan's victory, becoming the first Asian power to defeat a European power. <image:2464> ([https://www.britannica.com/event/Russo-Japanese-War](https://www.britannica.com/event/Russo-Japanese-War))


## Elaboration
The evidence provides historical context regarding conflicts between Russia, China, and Japan. Specifically, it mentions the Soviet invasion of Manchuria in 1945, which led to the return of Manchuria and Inner Mongolia to China ([https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_invasion_of_Manchuria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_invasion_of_Manchuria), [https://www.history.com/this-day-in-history/august-8/soviets-declare-war-on-japan-invade-manchuria](https://www.history.com/this-day-in-history/august-8/soviets-declare-war-on-japan-invade-manchuria)). It also highlights the Russo-Japanese War (1904-1905), where Japan defeated Russia ([https://www.britannica.com/event/Russo-Japanese-War](https://www.britannica.com/event/Russo-Japanese-War)).

The evidence does not support the claim that China and Japan currently plan to invade the Russian Federation. The provided sources only describe historical events.

To verify the claim, information about current geopolitical relations and any existing plans or intentions of China and Japan regarding Russia would be needed.

# Search Result
From [Source](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/China%E2%80%93Japan_relations): 
Content: "Japan has also condemned China's assertiveness in regional affairs and its cooperation with Russia, while both nations seek ways to improve diplomatic and economic ties.[\[74\]](#cite_note-74)

East China Sea
--------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=China%E2%80%93Japan_relations&action=edit&section=18 "Edit section: East China Sea")\
\]

Main article: [Senkaku Islands dispute](/wiki/Senkaku_Islands_dispute "Senkaku Islands dispute")

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Senkaku_Diaoyu_Tiaoyu_Islands.png/250px-Senkaku_Diaoyu_Tiaoyu_Islands.png)](/wiki/File:Senkaku_Diaoyu_Tiaoyu_Islands.png)

Location of Senkaku Islands

Both China and Japan claim sovereignty over [East China Sea](/wiki/East_China_Sea "East China Sea")
 islets that Japan calls the [Senkaku Islands](/wiki/Senkaku_Islands "Senkaku Islands")
 and China calls the Diaoyu Islands.

In August 1990, tensions over the islands between Japan, the PRC, and the ROC rose after Japanese media reported that the Japanese Maritime Safety Agency was preparing to recognize (as an official navigation mark) a lighthouse that a right-wing Japanese group built on the main island of the disputed island group.[\[75\]](#cite_note-:Wang-75)
: 258  PRC Vice Foreign Minister [Qi Huaiyuan](/wiki/Qi_Huaiyuan "Qi Huaiyuan")
 met with the Japanese Ambassador, reiterated the PRC's position of sovereignty over the islands, and stating that the two countries should shelve the dispute and look for opportunities to jointly develop resources in the area.[\[75\]](#cite_note-:Wang-75)
: 259  On 30 October 1990, the PRC and Japan stopped disputing the lighthouse issue.[\[75\]](#cite_note-:Wang-75)
: 259 

In 2005, clashes between Taiwanese (Chinese) protesters and the Japanese government in April 2005 led to anti-Japanese protests and sporadic violence across the PRC, from Beijing to Shanghai, later [Guangzhou](/wiki/Guangzhou "Guangzhou")
, [Shenzhen](/wiki/Shenzhen "Shenzhen")
 and [Shenyang](/wiki/Shenyang "Shenyang")
.[\[76\]](#cite_note-76)

In 2025, the East China Sea remains a flashpoint due to territorial disputes over the Senkaku Islands, claimed by both nations. Hardcover.

From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia

This article is about relations between the People's Republic of China and Japan. For historical relations between imperial China and imperial Japan, see [History of China–Japan relations](/wiki/History_of_China%E2%80%93Japan_relations "History of China–Japan relations")
. For relations between Japan and the Republic of China (Taiwan), see [Japan–Taiwan relations](/wiki/Japan%E2%80%93Taiwan_relations "Japan–Taiwan relations")
.

**China–Japan relations**, or [Sino](/wiki/Sinosphere "Sinosphere")
\-[Japanese](/wiki/Japan "Japan")
 relations, refer to the diplomatic, economic, and historical ties between the two nations, separated by the [East China Sea](/wiki/East_China_Sea "East China Sea")
. While efforts have been made to improve relations, longstanding disagreements remain.[\[2\]](#cite_note-:0-2)
[\[3\]](#cite_note-Ref_ac-3)
[\[4\]](#cite_note-4)

Background
----------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=China%E2%80%93Japan_relations&action=edit&section=1 "Edit section: Background")\
\]

Main articles: [History of China-Japan relations](/wiki/History_of_China-Japan_relations "History of China-Japan relations")
, [First Sino-Japanese War](/wiki/First_Sino-Japanese_War "First Sino-Japanese War")
, [Japanese invasion of Manchuria](/wiki/Japanese_invasion_of_Manchuria "Japanese invasion of Manchuria")
, and [Second Sino-Japanese War](/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War "Second Sino-Japanese War")

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Kibino_Makibi_Monument.jpg/250px-Kibino_Makibi_Monument.jpg)](/wiki/File:Kibino_Makibi_Monument.jpg)

Monument dedicated to [Kibi no Makibi](/wiki/Kibi_no_Makibi "Kibi no Makibi")
, Japanese diplomat who lived in China for 17 years.

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/PM_Kishida_meeting_with_President_Xi_%282023%29_01.jpg/250px-PM_Kishida_meeting_with_President_Xi_%282023%29_01.jpg)](/wiki/File:PM_Kishida_meeting_with_President_Xi_(2023)_01.jpg)

Japanese Prime Minister [Fumio Kishida](/wiki/Fumio_Kishida "Fumio Kishida")
 (left) and China's paramount leader [Xi Jinping](/wiki/Xi_Jinping "Xi Jinping")
 (right) [meet in San Francisco](/wiki/APEC_United_States_2023 "APEC United States 2023")
, United States in November 2023.

China and Japan are geographically separated only by a relatively narrow stretch of ocean. For a long time, there was trade and cultural contacts between the Japanese court and the Chinese nobility.\[_[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")\
_\]

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/LC-DIG-JPD-02538_%2817632626810%29.jpg/250px-LC-DIG-JPD-02538_%2817632626810%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:LC-DIG-JPD-02538_(17632626810).jpg)

The Japanese army launches a general offensive on [Tianjin](/wiki/Tianjin "Tianjin")
 castle during the [Boxer Rebellion](/wiki/Boxer_Rebellion "Boxer Rebellion")
, 1900.

When Western countries forced Japan to open trading in the mid-19th century, Japan moved towards modernization (Meiji Restoration), viewing China as an antiquated civilization, unable to defend itself against Western forces in part due to the First and Second Opium Wars along with the [Eight-Nation Alliance](/wiki/Eight-Nation_Alliance "Eight-Nation Alliance")
's involvement in suppressing the [Boxer Rebellion](/wiki/Boxer_Rebellion "Boxer Rebellion")
.\[_[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")\
_\]

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/First_pictures_of_the_Japanese_occupation_of_Peiping_in_China.jpg/250px-First_pictures_of_the_Japanese_occupation_of_Peiping_in_China.jpg)](/wiki/File:First_pictures_of_the_Japanese_occupation_of_Peiping_in_China.jpg)

Japanese march into [Zhengyangmen](/wiki/Zhengyangmen "Zhengyangmen")
 of [Beijing](/wiki/Beijing "Beijing")
 after capturing the city in July 1937

As a result of [Japanese war crimes](/wiki/Japanese_war_crimes "Japanese war crimes")
 during the [Second Sino-Japanese War](/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War "Second Sino-Japanese War")
 such as the [Nanjing massacre](/wiki/Nanjing_Massacre "Nanjing Massacre")
, and the Chinese view that Japan has not taken full responsibility for them, the bilateral relationship between China and Japan continues to be a sensitive issue in China.[\[5\]](#cite_note-:9-5)
: 24

## Evidence
### Evidence from `web_search`
The Soviet Union invaded Manchuria in August 1945, defeating the Japanese Kwantung Army, which led to the collapse of Japanese puppet states and the return of Manchuria and Inner Mongolia to China. The invasion also involved Mongolia and resulted in the capture of Japanese forces and looting by Soviet troops. ([https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_invasion_of_Manchuria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_invasion_of_Manchuria)) History.com published an article discussing the Soviet Union's declaration of war on Japan on August 8, 1945, and the subsequent invasion of Manchuria the following day <image:i>. ([https://www.history.com/this-day-in-history/august-8/soviets-declare-war-on-japan-invade-manchuria](https://www.history.com/this-day-in-history/august-8/soviets-declare-war-on-japan-invade-manchuria))

The Russo-Japanese War (1904-1905) between Japan and Russia, fought over dominance in Korea and Manchuria, resulted in Japan's victory, becoming the first Asian power to defeat a European power. <image:2464> ([https://www.britannica.com/event/Russo-Japanese-War](https://www.britannica.com/event/Russo-Japanese-War))


## Elaboration
The evidence provides historical context regarding conflicts between Russia, China, and Japan. Specifically, it mentions the Soviet invasion of Manchuria in 1945, which led to the return of Manchuria and Inner Mongolia to China ([https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_invasion_of_Manchuria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_invasion_of_Manchuria), [https://www.history.com/this-day-in-history/august-8/soviets-declare-war-on-japan-invade-manchuria](https://www.history.com/this-day-in-history/august-8/soviets-declare-war-on-japan-invade-manchuria)). It also highlights the Russo-Japanese War (1904-1905), where Japan defeated Russia ([https://www.britannica.com/event/Russo-Japanese-War](https://www.britannica.com/event/Russo-Japanese-War)).

The evidence does not support the claim that China and Japan currently plan to invade the Russian Federation. The provided sources only describe historical events.

Commentary

Relations With the Great Powers: Russia, Japan, China
=====================================================

##### 

Raymond L. Garthoff Former Brookings Expert

March 1, 1997

*   30 min read

*   [](https://twitter.com/intent/tweet?text=Relations+With+the+Great+Powers%3A+Russia%2C+Japan%2C+China&url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.brookings.edu%2Farticles%2Frelations-with-the-great-powers-russia-japan-china%2F%3Fb%3D1)

*   [](/cdn-cgi/l/email-protection#bc83cfc9ded6d9dfc881d4c8c8cccf869393cbcbcb92deced3d3d7d5d2dbcf92d9d8c986998e8ceed9d0ddc8d5d3d2cf998e8cebd5c8d4998e8cc8d4d9998e8cfbced9ddc8998e8cecd3cbd9cecf998ffd998e8ceec9cfcfd5dd998eff998e8cf6ddccddd2998eff998e8cffd4d5d2dd9aded3d8c581eed9d0ddc8d5d3d2cf998e8cebd5c8d4998e8cc8d4d9998e8cfbced9ddc8998e8cecd3cbd9cecf998ffd998e8ceec9cfcfd5dd998eff998e8cf6ddccddd2998eff998e8cffd4d5d2dd998cf8998cfd998cf8998cfdfeced3d3d7d5d2dbcf998e8ceed9cad5d9cb998e8cddcec8d5dfd0d9998e8cdec5998e8ceeddc5d1d3d2d8998e8cf092998e8cfbddcec8d4d3dada998e8c998e84efccced5d2db998e8c8d85858b998e85998cf8998cfd998cf8998cfdd4c8c8cccf998ffd998efa998efacbcbcb92deced3d3d7d5d2dbcf92d9d8c9998efaddcec8d5dfd0d9cf998efaced9d0ddc8d5d3d2cf91cbd5c8d491c8d4d991dbced9ddc891ccd3cbd9cecf91cec9cfcfd5dd91d6ddccddd291dfd4d5d2dd998efa998ffade998ff88d)
    

Print

Expansion of NATO—or, as its advocates now prefer to term it, NATO enlargement—is the most important international issue on the agenda today. The “regional cooperation” section of the April 1996 U.S.-Japan Joint Declaration on Security did nothing more than list in general terms common regional security goals regarding Korea, China, Russia, and Southeast Asia. Any restrictions on the freedoms of speech, press, or organization after July 1 could touch off a crisis in Sino-American relations, especially if the strictures involved the visible suppression of political protest.

In addition, China’s trade surplus with the United States, at least as measured by official American statistics, will probably exceed Japan’s trade surplus with the United States this year. In line with our [values and policies](/about-us/research-independence-and-integrity-policies/)
, each Brookings publication represents the sole views of its author(s).

[Support for Israel continues to deteriorate, especially among Democrats and young people](https://www.brookings.edu/articles/support-for-israel-continues-to-deteriorate-especially-among-democrats-and-young-people/)

!People take part in a protest against the Israeli government, demanding the release of all hostages, amid the ongoing conflict in Gaza between Israel and Hamas, outside the Israeli consulate in New York City, U.S. Moreover, we could facilitate that reluctant acceptance by rhetorical reassurances and various steps to assuage hurt Russian feelings by elaborating cooperative relations between NATO and Russia.

Opposition to expansion of NATO is, regrettably, the one thing on which virtually all Russian political figures can agree. But proceeding on the present track may be even more destabilizing.

The present course now includes an attempt to negotiate a NATO-Russian “charter” or other agreement, offering a yet undefined security relationship short of Russian membership in NATO. Above all, we should keep in mind that the objective is broader and deeper security, not expanding an organization for some at the cost of diminishing security for all.

**JAPAN**

**by Mike Mochizuki**

The post-World War II security relationship between Japan and the United States was based on a bargain inspired by the Soviet threat: the United States agreed to defend Japan in exchange for access to military bases in Japan. Since the Cold War’s end, Washington and Tokyo have been inching toward updating that paternalistic relationship not only to make it more reciprocal but also to expand its focus to include regional peace and stability.

Domestic pressures in both Japan and the United States argue for redefining the alliance. Washington and Tokyo must broaden the discussion to the coordination of diplomacy and economic policy to nurture a more benign regional environment.

**A New Consensus at Home**

Transforming the U.S.-Japan security relationship into a true alliance will require first of all forging a new domestic consensus in both Japan and the United States.

Recent trends in Japan present an opportunity to mobilize political support for a more activist security policy."

# Your Summary



===== > RESPONSE:  < =====
The Brookings article "Relations With the Great Powers: Russia, Japan, China" from March 1, 1997, discusses the security relationship between Japan and the United States, and mentions regional security goals regarding Korea, China, Russia, and Southeast Asia. The article also mentions the post-World War II security relationship between Japan and the United States, which was based on the Soviet threat. The article does not provide any information about current plans for China and Japan to invade Russia.

JudgePrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
**Determine the Claim's veracity** by following these steps:
1. Briefly summarize the key insights from the fact-check (see Record) in at most one paragraph.
2. Write one paragraph about which one of the Decision Options applies best. Include the most appropriate decision option at the end and enclose it in backticks like `this`.



## Decision Options
* `false`: The claim is not factually accurate. This is the case if one of the following three conditions is met:(1) The claim is demonstrably false when it is disproven by evidence from multiple and reliable sources,(2) The claim or image is taken out of context, i.e. the origin, content and/or meaning of a statement or an image is misrepresented. For example, an old claim or an old image is mispresented in a new context in a misleading way,(3) There is not enough evidence to verify the claim or the evidence is conflicting or self-contradictory.
* `not enough information`: The fact-check does not contain sufficient information to come to an conclusion. For example,there is substantial lack of evidence or the evidence is inconclusive, conflicting or self-contradictory. In the case of a lack of evidence, state which information exactly is missing. In particular, if no RESULTS or sources are available, pick this decision.
* `true`: The claim is factually accurate when it is confirmed by evidence from multiple and reliable sources.

# Instructions
The available knowledge is insufficient to assess the Claim. Therefore, **propose a set of actions** to retrieve new and helpful evidence. Adhere to the following rules:
* The actions available are listed under Valid Actions, including a short description for each action. No other actions are possible at this moment. 
* For each action, use the formatting as specified in Valid Actions.
* Include all actions in a single Markdown code block at the end of your answer.
* Propose as few actions as possible, but as much as needed. Do not propose similar or previously used actions.



## Valid Actions
* `reverse_search`
   * Description: Performs a reverse image search to find similar images on the web.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will perform a reverse search to find similar images.
   * Format: reverse_search(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `image_search`
   * Description: Run an image search on Google to retrieve related images for a given query.
   * How to use: This is a helpful tool for fact-checking images. Use this to retrieve images associated with a specific keyword or phrase. Ensure that the query is clear and specific to improve search accuracy. If no relevant images are found, refine the query or use more descriptive terms.
   * Format: image_search("your image search query goes here")

* `geolocate`
   * Description: Performs geolocation to determine the country where an image was taken.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will determine the most likely countries where it was taken.
   * Format: geolocate(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `web_search`
   * Description: Run an open web search on Google or DuckDuckGO to retrieve any related webpage.
   * How to use: Do not use this with a previously used or similar query from previous web searches. If a previous web search did not yield any results, use a very different query.
   * Format: web_search("your web search query goes here")

In order to find evidence that helps your fact-check, you just ran a web search which yielded a Search Result. **Your task right now is to summarize the Search Result.** What to include:
* information that might be useful for the fact-check (see Record)
* relevant images (refer to images by inserting their reference <image:k>)
* if available: the release date as well as the author or the publisher (e.g. the media company) of the search result.

Do NOT include:
* advertisements
* any other information not related to the Record or the Claim

Additional rules:
* Do not add any additional information besides the information in the Search Result.
* If the Search Result doesn't contain any relevant information for the fact-checking work, simply print one word in capital letters: "NONE".
* Keep your writing style like in the Examples 1, 2 and 3 provided to you.
* Try to filter out relevant information even if the search result is in a different language.

You just retrieved web sources, each one summarized under "Web Sources". **Your task right now is to summarize the web source summaries.**

Always adhere to the following rules:
* Write only one to two paragraphs.
* Include all URLs from the listed sources. Format them as Markdown hyperlinks.
* Do not add any additional information besides the information in the summaries.
* Include references (<image:k>) to all relevant images.

The document from hklaw.com lists the committee assignments for the House of Representatives and the Senate for the 118th Congress.

* information that might be useful for the fact-check (see Record)
* relevant images (refer to images by inserting their reference <image:k>)
* if available: the release date as well as the author or the publisher (e.g. the media company) of the search result.

Do NOT include:
* advertisements
* any other information not related to the Record or the Claim

Additional rules:
* Do not add any additional information besides the information in the Search Result.
* If the Search Result doesn't contain any relevant information for the fact-checking work, simply print one word in capital letters: "NONE".
* Keep your writing style like in the Examples 1, 2 and 3 provided to you.
* Try to filter out relevant information even if the search result is in a different language.

WASHINGTON (AP) — For a few gripping minutes, Rep. Adam Schiff, the lead impeachment prosecutor against President Donald Trump, had made the restless Senate snap to attention.

Voice cracking as he spoke, Schiff made an impassioned plea late Thursday for removing Trump from office, framing the choice in moral terms."

# Your Summary



===== > RESPONSE:  < =====
The Associated Press published an article about Adam Schiff, mentioning his role as the lead impeachment prosecutor against Donald Trump. <image:i> The article states that Schiff has been a frequent target of conservatives since the then GOP-led House Intelligence Committee started investigating Trump’s ties to Russia in the 2016 election.

_________________________



DevelopPrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
You just retrieved new Evidence. Now, **analyze the Claim's veracity using the evidence**. Always adhere to the following rules:
* Focus on developing new insights. Do not repeat larger parts from the Record. Do not restate the Claim.
* Write down your thoughts step-by-step. Whenever necessary, you may elaborate in more detail.
* Depending on the topic's complexity, invest one to three paragraphs. The fewer, the better.
* If you find that there is insufficient information to verify the Claim, explicitly state what information is missing.
* If you cite web sources, always refer to them by including their URL as a Markdown hyperlink.
* **Use information only from the recorded evidence**: Avoid inserting information that is not implied by the evidence. You may use commonsense knowledge, though.

# Record
## Claim
Claim: "Majority Leader John Thune blocked Senator Adam Schiff's committee assignments because of his past work in the Russia investigation over Donald Trump."

## Actions
```
web_search("John Thune Adam Schiff committee assignments")
web_search("John Thune blocks Adam Schiff committee assignments Russia investigation")
```

## Evidence
### Evidence from `web_search`
The article from ACEC.org discusses the Senate committee assignments for the 119th Congress, mentioning that Senator Adam Schiff (D-CA) was assigned to the Finance Committee and that Senate Republican Leader John Thune (R-SD) and Democratic Leader Chuck Schumer (D-NY) announced the committee assignments. [<image:2574>] and [<image:1>] The document from torreydc.com lists the Senate Committee Assignments for the 119th Congress, with Adam Schiff (D-CA) assigned to several committees and John Thune (R-SD) assigned to others; it does not mention any blocking of committee assignments. The document from hklaw.com lists the committee assignments for the House of Representatives and the Senate for the 118th Congress.

*   [https://www.acec.org/news/last-word-blog/post/senate-leaders-finalize-committee-assignments-for-the-119th-congress/](https://www.acec.org/news/last-word-blog/post/senate-leaders-finalize-committee-assignments-for-the-119th-congress/)
*   [https://torreydc.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/01/Senate-Committee-Assignments\_119-Congress\_Printable.pdf](https://torreydc.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/01/Senate-Committee-Assignments_119-Congress_Printable.pdf)
*   [https://www.hklaw.com/-/media/files/insights/eyes/2023/02/118thcongresscommitteeassignments.pdf](https://www.hklaw.com/-/media/files/insights/eyes/2023/02/118thcongresscommitteeassignments.pdf)


### Evidence from `web_search`
From [Source](https://apnews.com/article/donald-trump-ap-top-news-ca-state-wire-adam-schiff-politics-3eec3ea9be5c07a9c297bad439f8f3e8): 
Content: The Associated Press published an article about Adam Schiff, mentioning his role as the lead impeachment prosecutor against Donald Trump. <image:i> The article states that Schiff has been a frequent target of conservatives since the then GOP-led House Intelligence Committee started investigating Trump’s ties to Russia in the 2016 election.


# Your Analysis



===== > RESPONSE:  < =====
The evidence does not support the claim that John Thune blocked Adam Schiff's committee assignments. The provided sources mention committee assignments for the 119th and 118th Congresses, with Schiff being assigned to committees. The evidence does not mention any blocking by Thune. The AP article mentions Schiff's role in the Russia investigation, but it does not link this to any blocking of committee assignments.

To verify the claim, information is missing about whether Thune had the power to block Schiff's assignments and whether he actually did so. Also, it is missing whether the reason for blocking was Schiff's past work in the Russia investigation.

_________________________



JudgePrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
**Determine the Claim's veracity** by following these steps:
1. Briefly summarize the key insights from the fact-check (see Record) in at most one paragraph.
2. Write one paragraph about which one of the Decision Options applies best. Include the most appropriate decision option at the end and enclose it in backticks like `this`.



## Decision Options
* `false`: The claim is not factually accurate. This is the case if one of the following three conditions is met:(1) The claim is demonstrably false when it is disproven by evidence from multiple and reliable sources,(2) The claim or image is taken out of context, i.e. the origin, content and/or meaning of a statement or an image is misrepresented. For example, an old claim or an old image is mispresented in a new context in a misleading way,(3) There is not enough evidence to verify the claim or the evidence is conflicting or self-contradictory.
* `not enough information`: The fact-check does not contain sufficient information to come to an conclusion. For example,there is substantial lack of evidence or the evidence is inconclusive, conflicting or self-contradictory. In the case of a lack of evidence, state which information exactly is missing. In particular, if no RESULTS or sources are available, pick this decision.
* `true`: The claim is factually accurate when it is confirmed by evidence from multiple and reliable sources.

[<image:2574>] and [<image:1>] The document from torreydc.com lists the Senate Committee Assignments for the 119th Congress, with Adam Schiff (D-CA) assigned to several committees and John Thune (R-SD) assigned to others; it does not mention any blocking of committee assignments. The document from hklaw.com lists the committee assignments for the House of Representatives and the Senate for the 118th Congress.

### Evidence from `web_search`
From [Source](https://apnews.com/article/donald-trump-ap-top-news-ca-state-wire-adam-schiff-politics-3eec3ea9be5c07a9c297bad439f8f3e8): 
Content: The Associated Press published an article about Adam Schiff, mentioning his role as the lead impeachment prosecutor against Donald Trump. <image:i> The article states that Schiff has been a frequent target of conservatives since the then GOP-led House Intelligence Committee started investigating Trump’s ties to Russia in the 2016 election.


## Elaboration
The evidence does not support the claim that John Thune blocked Adam Schiff's committee assignments. The provided sources mention committee assignments for the 119th and 118th Congresses, with Schiff being assigned to committees. The evidence does not mention any blocking by Thune. The AP article mentions Schiff's role in the Russia investigation, but it does not link this to any blocking of committee assignments.

To verify the claim, information is missing about whether Thune had the power to block Schiff's assignments and whether he actually did so. Also, it is missing whether the reason for blocking was Schiff's past work in the Russia investigation.

PlanPrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
The available knowledge is insufficient to assess the Claim. Therefore, **propose a set of actions** to retrieve new and helpful evidence. Adhere to the following rules:
* The actions available are listed under Valid Actions, including a short description for each action. No other actions are possible at this moment. 
* For each action, use the formatting as specified in Valid Actions.
* Include all actions in a single Markdown code block at the end of your answer.
* Propose as few actions as possible, but as much as needed. Do not propose similar or previously used actions.



## Valid Actions
* `reverse_search`
   * Description: Performs a reverse image search to find similar images on the web.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will perform a reverse search to find similar images.
   * Format: reverse_search(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `image_search`
   * Description: Run an image search on Google to retrieve related images for a given query.
   * How to use: This is a helpful tool for fact-checking images. Use this to retrieve images associated with a specific keyword or phrase. Ensure that the query is clear and specific to improve search accuracy. If no relevant images are found, refine the query or use more descriptive terms.
   * Format: image_search("your image search query goes here")

* `geolocate`
   * Description: Performs geolocation to determine the country where an image was taken.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will determine the most likely countries where it was taken.
   * Format: geolocate(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `web_search`
   * Description: Run an open web search on Google or DuckDuckGO to retrieve any related webpage.
   * How to use: Do not use this with a previously used or similar query from previous web searches. If a previous web search did not yield any results, use a very different query.
   * Format: web_search("your web search query goes here")

# Instructions
In order to find evidence that helps your fact-check, you just ran a web search which yielded a Search Result. **Your task right now is to summarize the Search Result.** What to include:
* information that might be useful for the fact-check (see Record)
* relevant images (refer to images by inserting their reference <image:k>)
* if available: the release date as well as the author or the publisher (e.g. the media company) of the search result.

Do NOT include:
* advertisements
* any other information not related to the Record or the Claim

Additional rules:
* Do not add any additional information besides the information in the Search Result.
* If the Search Result doesn't contain any relevant information for the fact-checking work, simply print one word in capital letters: "NONE".
* Keep your writing style like in the Examples 1, 2 and 3 provided to you.
* Try to filter out relevant information even if the search result is in a different language.

John Thune
==========

From Ballotpedia

John Thune

!Image of John Thune <image:4484>

[Republican Party](https://ballotpedia.org/Republican_Party)

Candidate, U.S. [Tim Johnson](/Tim_Johnson "Tim Johnson")
 (D-S.D.) by 532 votes.[\[6\]](#cite_note-6)

Thune won election to the [Senate](/United_States_Senate "United States Senate")
 in 2004, defeating Senate Minority Leader [Tom Daschle](/Tom_Daschle "Tom Daschle")
 (D-S.D.) 50.6%-49.4%.[\[7\]](#cite_note-7)
 He was re-elected unopposed in 2010 and won with more than 70% of the vote in both [2016](/United_States_Senate_election_in_South_Dakota,_2016 "United States Senate election in South Dakota, 2016")
 and [2022](/United_States_Senate_election_in_South_Dakota,_2022 "United States Senate election in South Dakota, 2022")
. border](#Mexico-U.S._border)

Biography
---------

Email [editor@ballotpedia.org](mailto:editor@ballotpedia.org?subject=Bio update for John Thune)
 to notify us of updates to this biography.

In 1983, Thune received his bachelor's degree from Biola University in La Mirada, California. For more information pertaining to Thune's voting record in the 113th Congress, please see the below sections.[\[169\]](#cite_note-169)

#### National security

##### John Brennan CIA nomination

 Thune voted against the confirmation of John Brennan as Director of the Central Intelligence Agency. Senate, South Dakota General Election, 2016**

# Instructions
In order to find evidence that helps your fact-check, you just ran a web search which yielded a Search Result. **Your task right now is to summarize the Search Result.** What to include:
* information that might be useful for the fact-check (see Record)
* relevant images (refer to images by inserting their reference <image:k>)
* if available: the release date as well as the author or the publisher (e.g. the media company) of the search result.

Do NOT include:
* advertisements
* any other information not related to the Record or the Claim

Additional rules:
* Do not add any additional information besides the information in the Search Result.
* If the Search Result doesn't contain any relevant information for the fact-checking work, simply print one word in capital letters: "NONE".
* Keep your writing style like in the Examples 1, 2 and 3 provided to you.
* Try to filter out relevant information even if the search result is in a different language.

# Example 1
The search result from America Today provides several photographs of the Notre-Dame Cathedral fire on April 15, 2019. <image:i>, <image:j>, <image:k>. None of the images show the Eiffel Tower in the background.
