# Record
## Claim
Claim: "Majority Leader John Thune blocked Senator Adam Schiff's committee assignments because of his past work in the Russia investigation over Donald Trump."

## Actions
```
web_search("John Thune Adam Schiff committee assignments")
web_search("John Thune blocks Adam Schiff committee assignments Russia investigation")
```

## Evidence
### Evidence from `web_search`
The article from ACEC.org discusses the Senate committee assignments for the 119th Congress, mentioning that Senator Adam Schiff (D-CA) was assigned to the Finance Committee and that Senate Republican Leader John Thune (R-SD) and Democratic Leader Chuck Schumer (D-NY) announced the committee assignments. [<image:2574>] and [<image:1>] The document from torreydc.com lists the Senate Committee Assignments for the 119th Congress, with Adam Schiff (D-CA) assigned to several committees and John Thune (R-SD) assigned to others; it does not mention any blocking of committee assignments. The document from hklaw.com lists the committee assignments for the House of Representatives and the Senate for the 118th Congress.

*   [https://www.acec.org/news/last-word-blog/post/senate-leaders-finalize-committee-assignments-for-the-119th-congress/](https://www.acec.org/news/last-word-blog/post/senate-leaders-finalize-committee-assignments-for-the-119th-congress/)
*   [https://torreydc.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/01/Senate-Committee-Assignments\_119-Congress\_Printable.pdf](https://torreydc.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/01/Senate-Committee-Assignments_119-Congress_Printable.pdf)
*   [https://www.hklaw.com/-/media/files/insights/eyes/2023/02/118thcongresscommitteeassignments.pdf](https://www.hklaw.com/-/media/files/insights/eyes/2023/02/118thcongresscommitteeassignments.pdf)


### Evidence from `web_search`
From [Source](https://apnews.com/article/donald-trump-ap-top-news-ca-state-wire-adam-schiff-politics-3eec3ea9be5c07a9c297bad439f8f3e8): 
Content: The Associated Press published an article about Adam Schiff, mentioning his role as the lead impeachment prosecutor against Donald Trump. <image:i> The article states that Schiff has been a frequent target of conservatives since the then GOP-led House Intelligence Committee started investigating Trump’s ties to Russia in the 2016 election.


## Elaboration
The evidence does not support the claim that John Thune blocked Adam Schiff's committee assignments. The provided sources mention committee assignments for the 119th and 118th Congresses, with Schiff being assigned to committees. The evidence does not mention any blocking by Thune. The AP article mentions Schiff's role in the Russia investigation, but it does not link this to any blocking of committee assignments.

To verify the claim, information is missing about whether Thune had the power to block Schiff's assignments and whether he actually did so. Also, it is missing whether the reason for blocking was Schiff's past work in the Russia investigation.


## Actions
```
web_search("John Thune power to assign committee assignments")
web_search("Adam Schiff committee assignments blocked by John Thune")
```

# Search Result
From [Source](https://www.deseret.com/utah/2024/12/23/senate-committee-assignments-119th-congress/): 
Content: "Mike Lee will now have influence over important energy-related policies as chair of the Senate Energy and Natural Resources Committee.

Lee will also be joined on one of his committee assignments by freshman Sen.-elect John Curtis.

Late last week, incoming Senate Majority leader John Thune, R-S.D., released the list of GOP Senate committee assignments for the 119th Congress.

According to the [press release](https://www.thune.senate.gov/public/index.cfm/press-releases?ID=35D445C9-906D-4766-B50E-75E53D511A31)
 from Thune’s office, “The assignments have been ratified by the Senate Republican Conference and are expected to be ratified by the full Senate early next Congress.”

As the Senate changes from a Democratic to a Republican majority, major changes are being made in leadership and committee assignments.

“Seniority broadly dictates which Republicans are in line for these top posts, although they are technically voted on by the committee membership and then that is ratified by the full Republican conference and on the Senate floor,” according to [CNN.](https://www.cnn.com/2024/11/08/politics/gop-senate-committees-new-congress/index.html)

Related

[Government shutdown avoided, Sens. Lee and Curtis be on?

Lee, who is in his third term in the Senate, will serve as the chairman of the Energy and Natural Resources Committee, according to a post from the senator on [X.](https://x.com/SenMikeLee/status/1870523447098675336)

This position will “give him power over key issues important to his home state of Utah and a front-row seat to set energy policies that Republicans plan to champion in the next Congress,” according to [CNN.](https://www.cnn.com/2024/11/08/politics/gop-senate-committees-new-congress/index.html)

He will also sit on the Senate Judiciary, Foreign Relations and Budget committees.

“It is an honor to serve the people of Utah,” Lee wrote on [X](https://x.com/SenMikeLee/status/1870523447098675336)
 in regards to his committee assignments.

Curtis will join Lee on the Foreign Relations Committee, according to the [press release](https://www.thune.senate.gov/public/index.cfm/press-releases?ID=35D445C9-906D-4766-B50E-75E53D511A31)
 from Thune’s office.

Curtis will also sit on the Senate Environment and Public Works, Commerce, and Small Business committees.

“Tackling inflation, unlocking American energy, combatting global instability, and supporting small businesses are priorities Utahns have asked me to address,” Curtis said, according to a press release from his office. Mike Crapo will serve as the chairman of the Finance Committee, per the [press release.](https://www.thune.senate.gov/public/index.cfm/press-releases?ID=35D445C9-906D-4766-B50E-75E53D511A31)

Crapo will also sit on the Senate Banking; Health, Education, Labor, and Pensions; Judiciary; and Aging and Budget committees.

Idaho’s other senator, Jim Risch, will be the chair of the Foreign Relations Committee, which Lee and Curtis are both on.

According to Thune’s press release, Risch has also been assigned to sit on the Senate Energy, Intel, Small Business, and Ethics committees.

### Other notable committee assignments

Two other outspoken and well-known Republican senators, Ted Cruz and Rand Paul, have been named as the chairs of powerful committees.

“Cruz, Lee and Paul have often railed against Senate GOP leadership — and committee chairs — over government funding, deficit spending and other hot-button issues,“ according to CNN. [Utah](https://www.deseret.com/utah/)

DevelopPrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
You just retrieved new Evidence. Now, **analyze the Claim's veracity using the evidence**. Always adhere to the following rules:
* Focus on developing new insights. Do not repeat larger parts from the Record. Do not restate the Claim.
* Write down your thoughts step-by-step. Whenever necessary, you may elaborate in more detail.
* Depending on the topic's complexity, invest one to three paragraphs. The fewer, the better.
* If you find that there is insufficient information to verify the Claim, explicitly state what information is missing.
* If you cite web sources, always refer to them by including their URL as a Markdown hyperlink.
* **Use information only from the recorded evidence**: Avoid inserting information that is not implied by the evidence. You may use commonsense knowledge, though.

JudgePrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
**Determine the Claim's veracity** by following these steps:
1. Briefly summarize the key insights from the fact-check (see Record) in at most one paragraph.
2. Write one paragraph about which one of the Decision Options applies best. Include the most appropriate decision option at the end and enclose it in backticks like `this`.



## Decision Options
* `false`: The claim is not factually accurate. This is the case if one of the following three conditions is met:(1) The claim is demonstrably false when it is disproven by evidence from multiple and reliable sources,(2) The claim or image is taken out of context, i.e. the origin, content and/or meaning of a statement or an image is misrepresented. For example, an old claim or an old image is mispresented in a new context in a misleading way,(3) There is not enough evidence to verify the claim or the evidence is conflicting or self-contradictory.
* `not enough information`: The fact-check does not contain sufficient information to come to an conclusion. For example,there is substantial lack of evidence or the evidence is inconclusive, conflicting or self-contradictory. In the case of a lack of evidence, state which information exactly is missing. In particular, if no RESULTS or sources are available, pick this decision.
* `true`: The claim is factually accurate when it is confirmed by evidence from multiple and reliable sources.

# Record
## Claim
Claim: "Majority Leader John Thune blocked Senator Adam Schiff's committee assignments because of his past work in the Russia investigation over Donald Trump."

## Actions
```
web_search("John Thune Adam Schiff committee assignments")
web_search("John Thune blocks Adam Schiff committee assignments Russia investigation")
```

## Evidence
### Evidence from `web_search`
The article from ACEC.org discusses the Senate committee assignments for the 119th Congress, mentioning that Senator Adam Schiff (D-CA) was assigned to the Finance Committee and that Senate Republican Leader John Thune (R-SD) and Democratic Leader Chuck Schumer (D-NY) announced the committee assignments. ## Elaboration
The evidence does not support the claim that John Thune blocked Adam Schiff's committee assignments. The provided sources mention committee assignments for the 119th and 118th Congresses, with Schiff being assigned to committees. The evidence does not mention any blocking by Thune. The AP article mentions Schiff's role in the Russia investigation, but it does not link this to any blocking of committee assignments.

## Elaboration

PlanPrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
The available knowledge is insufficient to assess the Claim. Therefore, **propose a set of actions** to retrieve new and helpful evidence. Adhere to the following rules:
* The actions available are listed under Valid Actions, including a short description for each action. No other actions are possible at this moment. 
* For each action, use the formatting as specified in Valid Actions.
* Include all actions in a single Markdown code block at the end of your answer.
* Propose as few actions as possible, but as much as needed. Do not propose similar or previously used actions.



## Valid Actions
* `reverse_search`
   * Description: Performs a reverse image search to find similar images on the web.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will perform a reverse search to find similar images.
   * Format: reverse_search(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `image_search`
   * Description: Run an image search on Google to retrieve related images for a given query.
   * How to use: This is a helpful tool for fact-checking images. Use this to retrieve images associated with a specific keyword or phrase. Ensure that the query is clear and specific to improve search accuracy. If no relevant images are found, refine the query or use more descriptive terms.
   * Format: image_search("your image search query goes here")

* `geolocate`
   * Description: Performs geolocation to determine the country where an image was taken.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will determine the most likely countries where it was taken.
   * Format: geolocate(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `web_search`
   * Description: Run an open web search on Google or DuckDuckGO to retrieve any related webpage.
   * How to use: Do not use this with a previously used or similar query from previous web searches. If a previous web search did not yield any results, use a very different query.
   * Format: web_search("your web search query goes here")

SummarizeResultPrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
In order to find evidence that helps your fact-check, you just ran a web search which yielded a Search Result. **Your task right now is to summarize the Search Result.** What to include:
* information that might be useful for the fact-check (see Record)
* relevant images (refer to images by inserting their reference <image:k>)
* if available: the release date as well as the author or the publisher (e.g. the media company) of the search result.

Do NOT include:
* advertisements
* any other information not related to the Record or the Claim

Additional rules:
* Do not add any additional information besides the information in the Search Result.
* If the Search Result doesn't contain any relevant information for the fact-checking work, simply print one word in capital letters: "NONE".
* Keep your writing style like in the Examples 1, 2 and 3 provided to you.
* Try to filter out relevant information even if the search result is in a different language.

The search result from America Today provides several photographs of the Notre-Dame Cathedral fire on April 15, 2019. <image:i>, <image:j>, <image:k>. None of the images show the Eiffel Tower in the background.

Content: "[Jump to content](#bodyContent)

American politician (born 1960)

| Member of the [U.S. The fact that we have questions about this is in itself harmful".[\[84\]](#cite_note-84)
 The next morning on Twitter, Trump called Schiff "Sleazy Adam Schiff, the totally biased Congressman looking into 'Russia'" and called the Russian collusion investigation "the Dem loss excuse".[\[85\]](#cite_note-85)
 Schiff responded on Twitter that the president's "comments and actions are beneath the dignity of the office".[\[86\]](#cite_note-86)

In December 2018, Schiff suggested that Trump associate [Roger Stone](/wiki/Roger_Stone "Roger Stone")
 might have lied to Congress, and said the transcript of his testimony should be forwarded to the Special Counsel.[\[87\]](#cite_note-87)
 In November 2019, Stone was convicted of lying to Congress.[\[88\]](#cite_note-88)

When he became chair of the House Intelligence Committee in 2019, Schiff embarked on a personal mission to investigate Trump's connections to Russia, separate from the Special Counsel investigation.[\[89\]](#cite_note-89)
 He came under fire when he demurred when asked if he would accept it if the Special Counsel's investigation concluded that Trump had not colluded with Russia, saying that he had great confidence in Mueller but that "there may be, for example, evidence of collusion or conspiracy that is clear and convincing, but not proof beyond a reasonable doubt", as is needed for a criminal conviction.[\[90\]](#cite_note-90)

On March 28, 2019, the nine Republican members of the House Intelligence Committee officially called for Schiff to resign due to his allegations that Trump's campaign colluded with Russians in the 2016 election.[\[91\]](#cite_note-91)
 Schiff responded by accusing the Republican members of tolerating "immoral" and "corrupt" conduct by Trump campaign members and administration appointees.[\[92\]](#cite_note-92)
[\[93\]](#cite_note-93)

##### Censure

On June 21, 2023, the House of Representatives [censured](/wiki/Censure_in_the_United_States "Censure in the United States")
 Schiff in a [party-line vote](/wiki/Party-line_vote "Party-line vote")
 on H.Res. recognition of the [Republic of Artsakh](/wiki/Republic_of_Artsakh "Republic of Artsakh")
, which was an [autonomous oblast](/wiki/Autonomous_oblasts_of_the_Soviet_Union "Autonomous oblasts of the Soviet Union")
 within the [Azerbaijan Soviet Socialist Republic](/wiki/Azerbaijan_Soviet_Socialist_Republic "Azerbaijan Soviet Socialist Republic")
 but has been under control of ethnic Armenian forces backed by Armenia since the end of a [separatist war](/wiki/Nagorno-Karabakh_conflict "Nagorno-Karabakh conflict")
 in 1994.[\[121\]](#cite_note-121)
 He reiterated that call in April 2023.[\[122\]](#cite_note-122)

#### Investigation into the January 6 attack on the Capitol

On July 1, 2021, Pelosi appointed nine members (seven Democrats and two Republicans) to the [Select Committee to Investigate the January 6 Attack on the United States Capitol](/wiki/United_States_House_Select_Committee_on_the_January_6_Attack "United States House Select Committee on the January 6 Attack")
, which included Schiff.

On June 21, 2022, Schiff led Day 4 of the committee's [public hearings](/wiki/United_States_House_Select_Committee_on_the_January_6_Attack_public_hearings "United States House Select Committee on the January 6 Attack public hearings")
, which included testimony from three Republican officials to whom Trump reached out after the election: Georgia secretary of state [Brad Raffensperger](/wiki/Brad_Raffensperger "Brad Raffensperger")
, his deputy Gabe Sterling, and Arizona House of Representatives speaker [Rusty Bowers](/wiki/Rusty_Bowers "Rusty Bowers")
.[\[123\]](#cite_note-123)
 The second half of the hearing focused on Trump supporters' harassment of and threats to Georgia poll worker [Wandrea' ArShaye Moss](/wiki/Wandrea%27_ArShaye_Moss "Wandrea' ArShaye Moss")
 and her family, which led her to quit her job and go into hiding.[\[124\]](#cite_note-124)

Schiff was interviewed after the hearing by reporters and called the testimony "enormously powerful".[\[125\]](#cite_note-125)
 He added, "The lie lives on, and with it so does the danger."

#### Ban on stock trading

Schiff supports a ban on stock trading by members of Congress.[\[126\]](#cite_note-126)
[\[127\]](#cite_note-127)

Campaign for appointment to be California's attorney general
------------------------------------------------------------

In early December 2020, President-elect [Joe Biden](/wiki/Joe_Biden "Joe Biden")
 announced he would nominate [Attorney General of California](/wiki/Attorney_General_of_California "Attorney General of California")
 [Xavier Becerra](/wiki/Xavier_Becerra "Xavier Becerra")
 for [Secretary of Health and Human Services](/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_Health_and_Human_Services "United States Secretary of Health and Human Services")
.[\[139\]](#cite_note-139)
 [_Axios_](/wiki/Axios_(website) "Axios (website)")
 reported in February 2021 that Schiff was lobbying Governor [Gavin Newsom](/wiki/Gavin_Newsom "Gavin Newsom")
 and his allies to appoint him as Attorney General,[\[140\]](#cite_note-140)
 with a reported endorsement from [Speaker](/wiki/Speaker_of_the_United_States_House_of_Representatives "Speaker of the United States House of Representatives")
 [Nancy Pelosi](/wiki/Nancy_Pelosi "Nancy Pelosi")
.[\[28\]](#cite_note-:0-28)

In response to Schiff's lobbying for the attorney general's post, 36 criminal and social justice groups, notably the [Black Lives Matter](/wiki/Black_Lives_Matter "Black Lives Matter")
 Los Angeles and [Long Beach](/wiki/Long_Beach,_California "Long Beach, California")
 chapters, wrote an open letter to Newsom expressing "strong opposition", citing his past support for "tough on crime" measures, though they also specified that their letter was not an endorsement of any other candidate.[\[31\]](#cite_note-:1-31)
 On March 24, 2021, Newsom announced he would appoint California state assemblyman [Rob Bonta](/wiki/Rob_Bonta "Rob Bonta")
, who took office on April 23.[\[141\]](#cite_note-141)
[\[142\]](#cite_note-142)

U.S. senator in the [118th United States Congress](/wiki/118th_United_States_Congress "118th United States Congress")
.

#### Food and agriculture

A member of the [Senate Agriculture Committee](/wiki/United_States_Senate_Committee_on_Agriculture,_Nutrition,_and_Forestry "United States Senate Committee on Agriculture, Nutrition, and Forestry")
, Schiff led a July 2025 letter signed by 32 Democratic senators urging committee leadership to exclude any provisions in the upcoming [farm bill](/wiki/United_States_farm_bill "United States farm bill")
 that would overturn the California farm [animal welfare](/wiki/Animal_welfare "Animal welfare")
 law [Proposition 12](/wiki/2018_California_Proposition_12 "2018 California Proposition 12")
, which restricts the sale of products from animals raised in intensive [battery cages](/wiki/Battery_cage "Battery cage")
, [gestation crates](/wiki/Gestation_crate "Gestation crate")
, and [veal crates](/wiki/Veal#Veal_crate "Veal")
.[\[152\]](#cite_note-152)
[\[153\]](#cite_note-153)

#### Foreign policy

Schiff supported the [2025 Israeli strikes on Iran](/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Israel_War "Iran–Israel War")
, claiming that [Israel](/wiki/Israel "Israel")
 could "not afford" to let [Iran develop a nuclear weapon](/wiki/Iran_and_weapons_of_mass_destruction "Iran and weapons of mass destruction")
.[\[154\]](#cite_note-154)

#### Committee assignments

*   [Committee on Agriculture, Nutrition, and Forestry](/wiki/United_States_Senate_Committee_on_Agriculture,_Nutrition,_and_Forestry "United States Senate Committee on Agriculture, Nutrition, and Forestry")
    
*   [Committee on Environment and Public Works](/wiki/United_States_Senate_Committee_on_Environment_and_Public_Works "United States Senate Committee on Environment and Public Works")
    
*   [Committee on Small Business and Entrepreneurship](/wiki/United_States_Senate_Committee_on_Small_Business_and_Entrepreneurship "United States Senate Committee on Small Business and Entrepreneurship")
    
*   [Committee on the Judiciary](/wiki/United_States_Senate_Committee_on_the_Judiciary "United States Senate Committee on the Judiciary")

Adam and Eve Schiff

| Born | Adam Bennett Schiff<br><br>  <br>(1960-06-22) June 22, 1960 (age 65)  <br>[Framingham, Massachusetts](/wiki/Framingham,_Massachusetts "Framingham, Massachusetts")<br>, U.S. A resident of [Burbank](/wiki/Burbank,_California "Burbank, California")

 districts, all based in [Los Angeles County](/wiki/Los_Angeles_County,_California "Los Angeles County, California")
, during his time in the House of Representatives.

Schiff chaired the [House Intelligence Committee](/wiki/United_States_House_Permanent_Select_Committee_on_Intelligence "United States House Permanent Select Committee on Intelligence")
 from 2019 to 2023 before being removed from it by [Republican](/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States) "Republican Party (United States)")
 House speaker [Kevin McCarthy](/wiki/Kevin_McCarthy "Kevin McCarthy")

California State Senate (1996–2000)
-----------------------------------

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/60/Adam_Schiff.gif)](/wiki/File:Adam_Schiff.gif)

Schiff as a state senator in 1997

In 1996, Schiff was elected to represent the [21st district](/wiki/California%27s_21st_State_Senate_district "California's 21st State Senate district")
 in the [California State Senate](/wiki/California_State_Senate "California State Senate")
, defeating Republican assemblywoman [Paula Boland](/wiki/Paula_Boland "Paula Boland")
, who had moved into the district to run.[\[23\]](#cite_note-23)
[\[24\]](#cite_note-24)
 When his term began, he was the Senate's youngest member, at 36.[\[25\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTE''The_Jews_of_Capitol_Hill''465-25)
 During his four-year term, Schiff chaired the Senate Judiciary Committee and Select Committee on Juvenile Justice, and the state legislature's Joint Committee on the Arts.[\[25\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTE''The_Jews_of_Capitol_Hill''465-25)

As a state senator, Schiff authored dozens of measures that were enacted into law.[\[25\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTE''The_Jews_of_Capitol_Hill''465-25)
 These included Senate Bill 1847, Chapter 1021.[\[26\]](#cite_note-Coleman-26)
 Passed in 1998, this legislation continued work on the stalled Blue Line light rail extension to [Pasadena](/wiki/Pasadena,_California "Pasadena, California")
 by renaming the Blue Line the [Gold Line](/wiki/L_Line_(Los_Angeles_Metro) "L Line (Los Angeles Metro)")
[\[26\]](#cite_note-Coleman-26)
 and creating the Foothill Gold Line Construction Authority, which separated the project from the [Los Angeles County Metropolitan Transportation Authority](/wiki/Los_Angeles_County_Metropolitan_Transportation_Authority "Los Angeles County Metropolitan Transportation Authority")
.[\[27\]](#cite_note-Scauzillo-27)
 The construction authority finished the Pasadena line in 2003 and extended it to [Azusa](/wiki/Azusa,_California "Azusa, California")
 in 2016.[\[27\]](#cite_note-Scauzillo-27)
 A third leg was begun, which is intended to extend the line to [Pomona](/wiki/Pomona,_California "Pomona, California")
 by 2025.[\[27\]](#cite_note-Scauzillo-27)
 Schiff's work on the project earned him the nickname "Father of the Gold Line".[\[27\]](#cite_note-Scauzillo-27)

During his tenure, Schiff also authored "tough on crime" measures, which did not pass or were vetoed by governors, including a bill to allow minors 14 or older accused of serious crimes to be tried as adults[\[28\]](#cite_note-:0-28)
[\[29\]](#cite_note-29)
 and a bill that would have made it a felony to hire an [undocumented immigrant](/wiki/Undocumented_immigrant "Undocumented immigrant")
.[\[30\]](#cite_note-30)
[\[31\]](#cite_note-:1-31)
 According to _[The Guardian](/wiki/The_Guardian "The Guardian")
_, these proposals were in line with the "tough on crime" attitude of other politicians in the late 1990s.[\[28\]](#cite_note-:0-28)

U.S. citizen".[\[98\]](#cite_note-98)

In April 2018, when asked whether he thought Trump deserved at least partial credit for North Korea's involvement in talks with the U.S., Schiff replied: "I think it's more than fair to say that the combination of the president's unpredictability and indeed his bellicosity had something to do with the North Koreans deciding to come to the negotiating table".[\[99\]](#cite_note-99)

#### Israel and antisemitism

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Adam_Schiff_and_Ehud_Barak.jpg/250px-Adam_Schiff_and_Ehud_Barak.jpg)](/wiki/File:Adam_Schiff_and_Ehud_Barak.jpg)

Schiff with former Israeli Prime Minister [Ehud Barak](/wiki/Ehud_Barak "Ehud Barak")
 in 2002

Schiff is a supporter of [Israel](/wiki/Israel "Israel")
.[\[100\]](#cite_note-100)
 In December 2016, he urged Obama to veto [UN Security Council Resolution 2334](/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_2334 "United Nations Security Council Resolution 2334")
, which condemned [Israeli settlement building](/wiki/Israeli_settlement "Israeli settlement")
 in the occupied [Palestinian territories](/wiki/Palestinian_territories "Palestinian territories")
 as a violation of [international law](/wiki/International_law "International law")
.[\[101\]](#cite_note-101)

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/DAZ_3601PS_%2851885313883%29.jpg/250px-DAZ_3601PS_%2851885313883%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:DAZ_3601PS_(51885313883).jpg)

Schiff and [Nancy Pelosi](/wiki/Nancy_Pelosi "Nancy Pelosi")
 in the [Knesset](/wiki/Knesset "Knesset")
, Jerusalem, February 2022

In February 2019, Representative [Ilhan Omar](/wiki/Ilhan_Omar "Ilhan Omar")
 tweeted, "It's all about the Benjamins baby" in reference to American politicians' [support for Israel](/wiki/Israel_lobby_in_the_United_States "Israel lobby in the United States")
 and invoked the [American Israel Public Affairs Committee](/wiki/American_Israel_Public_Affairs_Committee "American Israel Public Affairs Committee")
 (AIPAC). Schiff said it was "never acceptable to give voice to, or repeat, anti-Semitic smears".[\[102\]](#cite_note-102)

In October 2023, Schiff condemned [Hamas](/wiki/Hamas "Hamas")
's actions during the [Gaza war](/wiki/Gaza_war "Gaza war")
 and expressed his support for Israel and its right to self-defense.[\[103\]](#cite_note-103)
 He rejected calls for a ceasefire but said he supported "humanitarian pauses" to deliver aid to Palestinians in the [Gaza Strip](/wiki/Gaza_Strip "Gaza Strip")
.[\[104\]](#cite_note-104)

The AIPAC-affiliated Super PAC, United Democracy Project, gave $5 million to the pro-Schiff superpac Standing Strong during Schiff's 2024 Senate primary campaign, as confirmed by its spokesman, Patrick Dorton.[\[105\]](#cite_note-105)
 Democratic Majority for Israel's political arm, DMFI PAC, also endorsed Schiff during this campaign.[\[106\]](#cite_note-106)

#### Murder of Jamal Khashoggi

After news reports that the [CIA](/wiki/CIA "CIA")
 concluded that Saudi crown prince [Mohammed bin Salman](/wiki/Mohammed_bin_Salman "Mohammed bin Salman")
 had ordered the assassination of Saudi journalist [Jamal Khashoggi](/wiki/Jamal_Khashoggi "Jamal Khashoggi")
, Trump said there was insufficient CIA evidence to link bin Salman to the murder.[\[107\]](#cite_note-107)
 As the top Democrat on the [House Intelligence Committee](/wiki/House_Intelligence_Committee "House Intelligence Committee")
, Schiff was briefed by the CIA on the agency assessment, and said afterward that Trump was being dishonest about the CIA findings.[\[108\]](#cite_note-108)

#### Impeachments

See also: [First impeachment of Donald Trump](/wiki/First_impeachment_of_Donald_Trump "First impeachment of Donald Trump")
, [First impeachment trial of Donald Trump](/wiki/First_impeachment_trial_of_Donald_Trump "First impeachment trial of Donald Trump")
, and [Impeachment inquiry against Donald Trump](/wiki/Impeachment_inquiry_against_Donald_Trump "Impeachment inquiry against Donald Trump")

In 2009, Schiff was appointed and served as an [impeachment manager](/wiki/Impeachment_manager "Impeachment manager")
 (prosecutor) in the [impeachment trial](/wiki/Federal_impeachment_trial_in_the_United_States "Federal impeachment trial in the United States")
 of Judge [Samuel B. Senate (2024–present)

# Instructions
You just retrieved new Evidence. Now, **analyze the Claim's veracity using the evidence**. Always adhere to the following rules:
* Focus on developing new insights. Do not repeat larger parts from the Record. Do not restate the Claim.
* Write down your thoughts step-by-step. Whenever necessary, you may elaborate in more detail.
* Depending on the topic's complexity, invest one to three paragraphs. The fewer, the better.
* If you find that there is insufficient information to verify the Claim, explicitly state what information is missing.
* If you cite web sources, always refer to them by including their URL as a Markdown hyperlink.
* **Use information only from the recorded evidence**: Avoid inserting information that is not implied by the evidence. You may use commonsense knowledge, though.

# Record
## Claim
Claim: "Majority Leader John Thune blocked Senator Adam Schiff's committee assignments because of his past work in the Russia investigation over Donald Trump."

## Actions
```
web_search("John Thune Adam Schiff committee assignments")
web_search("John Thune blocks Adam Schiff committee assignments Russia investigation")
```

## Evidence
### Evidence from `web_search`
The article from ACEC.org discusses the Senate committee assignments for the 119th Congress, mentioning that Senator Adam Schiff (D-CA) was assigned to the Finance Committee and that Senate Republican Leader John Thune (R-SD) and Democratic Leader Chuck Schumer (D-NY) announced the committee assignments. [<image:2574>] and [<image:1>] The document from torreydc.com lists the Senate Committee Assignments for the 119th Congress, with Adam Schiff (D-CA) assigned to several committees and John Thune (R-SD) assigned to others; it does not mention any blocking of committee assignments. The document from hklaw.com lists the committee assignments for the House of Representatives and the Senate for the 118th Congress.

*   [https://www.acec.org/news/last-word-blog/post/senate-leaders-finalize-committee-assignments-for-the-119th-congress/](https://www.acec.org/news/last-word-blog/post/senate-leaders-finalize-committee-assignments-for-the-119th-congress/)
*   [https://torreydc.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/01/Senate-Committee-Assignments\_119-Congress\_Printable.pdf](https://torreydc.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/01/Senate-Committee-Assignments_119-Congress_Printable.pdf)
*   [https://www.hklaw.com/-/media/files/insights/eyes/2023/02/118thcongresscommitteeassignments.pdf](https://www.hklaw.com/-/media/files/insights/eyes/2023/02/118thcongresscommitteeassignments.pdf)


### Evidence from `web_search`
From [Source](https://apnews.com/article/donald-trump-ap-top-news-ca-state-wire-adam-schiff-politics-3eec3ea9be5c07a9c297bad439f8f3e8): 
Content: The Associated Press published an article about Adam Schiff, mentioning his role as the lead impeachment prosecutor against Donald Trump. <image:i> The article states that Schiff has been a frequent target of conservatives since the then GOP-led House Intelligence Committee started investigating Trump’s ties to Russia in the 2016 election.


## Elaboration
The evidence does not support the claim that John Thune blocked Adam Schiff's committee assignments. The provided sources mention committee assignments for the 119th and 118th Congresses, with Schiff being assigned to committees. The evidence does not mention any blocking by Thune. The AP article mentions Schiff's role in the Russia investigation, but it does not link this to any blocking of committee assignments.

To verify the claim, information is missing about whether Thune had the power to block Schiff's assignments and whether he actually did so. Also, it is missing whether the reason for blocking was Schiff's past work in the Russia investigation.


## Actions
```
web_search("John Thune power to assign committee assignments")
web_search("Adam Schiff committee assignments blocked by John Thune")
```

## Evidence
### Evidence from `web_search`
The Ballotpedia article on John Thune lists his committee assignments and his role as Senate Republican Whip, but it does not mention him blocking Adam Schiff's committee assignments. [<image:4484>] The Deseret News article from December 23, 2024, discusses Senate committee assignments for the 119th Congress, stating that John Thune, as the incoming Senate Majority Leader, released the GOP Senate committee assignments, which are ratified by the Senate Republican Conference. The article does not mention Adam Schiff or any blocking of committee assignments.


## Elaboration
The evidence indicates that John Thune, as Senate Majority Leader, had a role in releasing GOP Senate committee assignments. However, the provided sources do not confirm that Thune blocked Adam Schiff's committee assignments. Therefore, the claim cannot be verified with the available information.

# Instructions

1. Briefly summarize the key insights from the fact-check (see Record) in at most one paragraph.
2. Write one paragraph about which one of the Decision Options applies best. Include the most appropriate decision option at the end and enclose it in backticks like `this`.



## Decision Options
* `false`: The claim is not factually accurate. This is the case if one of the following three conditions is met:(1) The claim is demonstrably false when it is disproven by evidence from multiple and reliable sources,(2) The claim or image is taken out of context, i.e. the origin, content and/or meaning of a statement or an image is misrepresented. For example, an old claim or an old image is mispresented in a new context in a misleading way,(3) There is not enough evidence to verify the claim or the evidence is conflicting or self-contradictory.
* `true`: The claim is factually accurate when it is confirmed by evidence from multiple and reliable sources.

## Final Judgement
The fact-check reveals that while John Thune had a role in releasing GOP Senate committee assignments, there is no evidence to support the claim that he blocked Adam Schiff's assignments. The evidence indicates that Schiff was removed from the House Intelligence Committee by Kevin McCarthy, but this is not related to Thune. Therefore, the claim is not supported by the available information. `false`


## Summary



===== > RESPONSE:  < =====
The available evidence does not support the claim. While John Thune had a role in releasing GOP Senate committee assignments, there is no evidence to suggest he blocked Adam Schiff's assignments. Furthermore, the evidence indicates that Schiff was removed from the House Intelligence Committee by Kevin McCarthy, not Thune.

PlanPrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
The available knowledge is insufficient to assess the Claim. Therefore, **propose a set of actions** to retrieve new and helpful evidence. Adhere to the following rules:
* The actions available are listed under Valid Actions, including a short description for each action. No other actions are possible at this moment. 
* For each action, use the formatting as specified in Valid Actions.
* Include all actions in a single Markdown code block at the end of your answer.
* Propose as few actions as possible, but as much as needed. Do not propose similar or previously used actions.



## Valid Actions
* `reverse_search`
   * Description: Performs a reverse image search to find similar images on the web.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will perform a reverse search to find similar images.
   * Format: reverse_search(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `image_search`
   * Description: Run an image search on Google to retrieve related images for a given query.
   * How to use: This is a helpful tool for fact-checking images. Use this to retrieve images associated with a specific keyword or phrase. Ensure that the query is clear and specific to improve search accuracy. If no relevant images are found, refine the query or use more descriptive terms.
   * Format: image_search("your image search query goes here")

* `geolocate`
   * Description: Performs geolocation to determine the country where an image was taken.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will determine the most likely countries where it was taken.
   * Format: geolocate(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `web_search`
   * Description: Run an open web search on Google or DuckDuckGO to retrieve any related webpage.
   * How to use: Do not use this with a previously used or similar query from previous web searches. If a previous web search did not yield any results, use a very different query.
   * Format: web_search("your web search query goes here")

Armed Forces Day (Poland)

[](#)

5 languages [Add topic](#) [Jump to content](#bodyContent)

From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia

National holiday in Poland

| Armed Forces Day |     |
| --- | --- |
| [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Polish_M1_Abrams.jpg/330px-Polish_M1_Abrams.jpg)](/wiki/File:Polish_M1_Abrams.jpg)<br><br>Armed Forces Day 2023, Warsaw |     |
| Official name | Święto Wojska Polskiego |
| Observed by | Poland |
| Significance | [Battle of Warsaw (1920)](/wiki/Battle_of_Warsaw_(1920) "Battle of Warsaw (1920)") |
| Celebrations | [Military parades](/wiki/Military_parade "Military parade")<br>, equipment reviews, silences |
| Begins | 13:00 [CET](/wiki/Central_European_Time "Central European Time") |
| Date | 15 August |
| Next time | 15 August 2025 (2025-08-15) |
| Frequency | annual |

**Armed Forces Day**, known also as the **Feast of the Polish Armed Forces** ([Polish](/wiki/Polish_language "Polish language")
: _Święto Wojska Polskiego_), is a national holiday celebrated annually on 15 August in Poland, commemorating the anniversary of the 1920 victory over [Soviet Russia](/wiki/Russian_Soviet_Federative_Socialist_Republic "Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic")
 at the [Battle of Warsaw](/wiki/Battle_of_Warsaw_(1920) "Battle of Warsaw (1920)")
 during the [Polish–Soviet War](/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Soviet_War "Polish–Soviet War")
.[\[1\]](#cite_note-PolskieRadio2013-1)
 Armed Forces Day is held in conjunction with the [Day of the Assumption of the Virgin Mary](/wiki/Assumption_of_Mary "Assumption of Mary")
, itself a separate public holiday.[\[2\]](#cite_note-Kontakt24-2)
 The event is marked by [military parades](/wiki/Military_parade "Military parade")
, equipment reviews, showcases and remembrances by all branches of the [Polish Armed Forces](/wiki/Polish_Armed_Forces "Polish Armed Forces")
 across the country. To commemorate the republic's victory over the Red Army, Minister of Military Affairs [Stanisław Szeptycki](/wiki/Stanis%C5%82aw_Szeptycki "Stanisław Szeptycki")
 established the Feast of the Soldier (_Święta Żołnierza_), or Soldiers Day, in 1923.[\[4\]](#cite_note-4)
 In proclaiming the holiday, Szeptycki declared that, "\[o\]n the anniversary of the memorable defeat of the Bolshevik onslaught on Warsaw, we honor the memory of those killed in battles with enemies throughout all ages and for Polish independence."[\[5\]](#cite_note-Museum-5)
 The date of 15 August was chosen as it coincided with the [21st Mountain Division's](/wiki/21st_Mountain_Infantry_Division_(Poland) "21st Mountain Infantry Division (Poland)")
 evening counterattack on Russian troops, eventually forcing the Red Army's general retreat.[\[2\]](#cite_note-Kontakt24-2)
 Additionally, the government of the Second Republic desired the military's greater integration with the new state, as well as for the armed forces to improve its image among the civilian public.[\[2\]](#cite_note-Kontakt24-2)

The Feast of the Soldier remained a celebrated holiday until 1947, when the newly installed communist government of the [People's Republic of Poland](/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_Poland "People's Republic of Poland")
 discontinued the tradition.[\[6\]](#cite_note-Gazeta2013-6)
 In 1950, the [Council of Ministers](/wiki/Cabinet_of_Poland "Cabinet of Poland")
 under Prime Minister [Józef Cyrankiewicz](/wiki/J%C3%B3zef_Cyrankiewicz "Józef Cyrankiewicz")
 passed regulations to officially celebrate the military on 12 October.[\[7\]](#cite_note-DzU1950-7)
 Renaming the celebration as Polish Armed Forces Day (_Dzień Wojska Polskiego_), the day marked the anniversary of the Soviet-organized [Polish 1st Tadeusz Kościuszko Infantry Division](/wiki/Polish_1st_Tadeusz_Ko%C5%9Bciuszko_Infantry_Division "Polish 1st Tadeusz Kościuszko Infantry Division")
 engaging [German](/wiki/Nazi_Germany "Nazi Germany")
 units at the [Battle of Lenino](/wiki/Battle_of_Lenino "Battle of Lenino")
 in October 1943.[\[7\]](#cite_note-DzU1950-7)
 The communist government found it impossible to celebrate the original date of 15 August and its coinciding historical significance, owing to its glorification of the [Red Army](/wiki/Red_Army "Red Army")
's defeat.[\[8\]](#cite_note-PolskieRadio2012-8)
 Following the return of democracy in the wake of the [events of 1989](/wiki/Revolutions_of_1989 "Revolutions of 1989")
, the [Sejm](/wiki/Sejm "Sejm")
 approved the restoration of Armed Forces Day to the original 15 August date and meaning on 30 July 1992, repealing the earlier communist era 1950 declaration.[\[9\]](#cite_note-Sejm1992-9)

Commemorations
--------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Armed_Forces_Day_(Poland)&action=edit&section=2 "Edit section: Commemorations")\
\]

Armed Forces Day is celebrated throughout Poland, with military parades, commemorations for active personnel, veterans, and the dead. As head of state and [commander-in-chief](/wiki/Commander-in-chief "Commander-in-chief")
, the [President of Poland](/wiki/President_of_Poland "President of Poland")
 presides over promotions of high-ranking officers, including the promotion of colonels to generals at the [Presidential Palace](/wiki/Presidential_Palace,_Warsaw "Presidential Palace, Warsaw")
.[\[1\]](#cite_note-PolskieRadio2013-1)
 The pageantry continues with commemorations near the [Tomb of the Unknown Soldier](/wiki/Tomb_of_the_Unknown_Soldier,_Warsaw "Tomb of the Unknown Soldier, Warsaw")
 held in [Piłsudski Square](/wiki/Pi%C5%82sudski_Square "Piłsudski Square")
.[\[11\]](#cite_note-Prezydent-11)
 The events in Warsaw typically involve the participation of the nation's political establishment, including the [president](/wiki/President_of_Poland "President of Poland")
, the [prime minister](/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Poland "Prime Minister of Poland")
, and leading members of the [cabinet](/wiki/Cabinet_of_Poland "Cabinet of Poland")
.[\[6\]](#cite_note-Gazeta2013-6)
 Leading politicians also lay wreaths at the [Józef Piłsudski](/wiki/J%C3%B3zef_Pi%C5%82sudski "Józef Piłsudski")
 Monument, as well as at the [Tomb of the Unknown Soldier](/wiki/Tomb_of_the_Unknown_Soldier,_Warsaw "Tomb of the Unknown Soldier, Warsaw")
.[\[6\]](#cite_note-Gazeta2013-6)

As a [NATO](/wiki/NATO "NATO")
 member state, Armed Forces Day in Poland typically draws representatives from other allied militaries in attendance.[\[12\]](#cite_note-12)

The centennial celebrations for 2020 were "1920 Battle of Warsaw – a Polish victory for the freedom of Europe".[\[13\]](#cite_note-13)

### Armed Forces Day Parade

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Armed_Forces_Day_(Poland)&action=edit&section=3 "Edit section: Armed Forces Day Parade")\
\]

One of the main attractions of the Warsaw festivities is a [military parade](/wiki/Military_parade "Military parade")
 of servicemen and women, as well as a review of existing military equipment, held normally along [Ujazdów Avenue](/wiki/Ujazd%C3%B3w_Avenue "Ujazdów Avenue")
.[\[11\]](#cite_note-Prezydent-11)
 Active servicemen and women participate at many events, joined often by volunteers appearing in historical dress, including those donning the equipment and dress of the [Polish–Soviet War](/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Soviet_War "Polish–Soviet War")
 or other historical periods.[\[1\]](#cite_note-PolskieRadio2013-1)
 The first grand military parades since the holiday was reinstated in Warsaw were in 2007 and 2008, and parades have been held yearly since 2013. In 2019, the parade took place in the southern city of [Katowice](/wiki/Katowice "Katowice")
 to honour the participation of [Silesia](/wiki/Silesia "Silesia")
's residents in the [Silesian Uprisings](/wiki/Silesian_Uprisings "Silesian Uprisings")
 from 1919 to 1921.[\[14\]](#cite_note-14)

14. One of the most prominent events of the day is in the capital Warsaw, which hosts a large military parade through the city's center. Originally celebrated during the [Second Republic](/wiki/Second_Polish_Republic "Second Polish Republic")
, the holiday was barred by authorities during the communist era beginning in 1947, only to be revived again in 1992.[\[3\]](#cite_note-3)

History
-------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Armed_Forces_Day_(Poland)&action=edit&section=1 "Edit section: History")\
\]

Main article: [Battle of Warsaw (1920)](/wiki/Battle_of_Warsaw_(1920) "Battle of Warsaw (1920)")

In the event known by the critics as the "Miracle of the Vistula," the [Polish Army](/wiki/Polish_Army "Polish Army")
 under the command of Marshal [Józef Piłsudski](/wiki/J%C3%B3zef_Pi%C5%82sudski "Józef Piłsudski")
 successfully repulsed a [Red Army](/wiki/Red_Army "Red Army")
 offensive outside of Warsaw in mid-August 1920. As the day coincides with the religious [Day of the Assumption](/wiki/Assumption_of_Mary "Assumption of Mary")
, church masses across the country reflect on the memory of Poland's military dead.[\[2\]](#cite_note-Kontakt24-2)
 Additionally, a number of military-themed events are held throughout many of the nation's larger towns and cities, including equipment demonstrations for the general public and open house events.[\[10\]](#cite_note-TVNWarszawa-10)

In Warsaw, the holiday is commemorated by several state events in the central [Śródmieście](/wiki/%C5%9Ar%C3%B3dmie%C5%9Bcie,_Warsaw "Śródmieście, Warsaw")
 borough of the capital."

Copyright© Polskie Radio S.A. 11, 2024.Photo: PAP/Radek Pietruszka

This year’s parade on August 15 will be an expression of "strength, agency and unity" in the face of "threats from the East," Defence Minister Władysław Kosiniak-Kamysz has said.

 ![Image:](//static.prsa.pl/images/0cef8818-5db9-4622-ab61-65537c098870.jpg)Image: Polish Ministry of Defence/gov.pl

Speaking during a rehearsal ahead of the Armed Forces Day parade in Warsaw, Kosiniak-Kamysz encouraged the public to celebrate the anniversary of Poland's "great victory" over the Russian Bolsheviks at the 1920 Battle of Warsaw.

"Our presence will be an expression of gratitude to past generations and hope for future ones," he said.

 ![Władysław Kosiniak-Kamysz ocenił, że droga prowadząca do zdejmowania krzyży w urzędach jest niewłaściwa](//static.prsa.pl/images/86a0288d-46e6-49d7-bf5f-25dc1130d796.jpg)Władysław Kosiniak-Kamysz. Photo: PAP/Marian Zubrzycki

"It will also show our strength, agency and unity in the face of threats from the East," he added.

> Ministerstwo Obrony Narodowej zaprasza na defiladę oraz do wspólnego obchodzenia Święta Wojska Polskiego! Zobaczymy ponad 80 statków… [pic.twitter.com/MBn6EXCkty](https://t.co/MBn6EXCkty)
> 
> — Ministerstwo Obrony Narodowej 🇵🇱 (@MON\_GOV\_PL) [July 29, 2024](https://twitter.com/MON_GOV_PL/status/1817930176384077866?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw)

Thursday's military parade in the Polish capital will showcase hardware including South Korean-made K2 battle tanks, Polish-produced 155 mm Krab self-propelled gun-howitzers, Kleszcz reconnaissance vehicles, K9 Thunder self-propelled howitzers from South Korea, and domestically produced Rosomak wheeled armoured personnel carriers, the Polish defence ministry said in an [announcement](https://www.gov.pl/web/obrona-narodowa/swieto-wojska-polskiego---zapraszamy-do-wojska).

Other weaponry will include US-made M1A1 Abrams tanks, HIMARS missile launchers, Black Hawk multi-role helicopters, and a Patriot medium-range air defence system.

> Zapraszamy do wspólnych obchodów [#ŚwiętoWojskaPolskiego](https://twitter.com/hashtag/%C5%9Awi%C4%99toWojskaPolskiego?src=hash&ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw)

Therefore, the claim is partially accurate regarding the date and the nature of the event but lacks evidence to support the claim that it was preparing for war with Russia.

## Decision Options
* `false`: The claim is not factually accurate. This is the case if one of the following three conditions is met:(1) The claim is demonstrably false when it is disproven by evidence from multiple and reliable sources,(2) The claim or image is taken out of context, i.e. the origin, content and/or meaning of a statement or an image is misrepresented. For example, an old claim or an old image is mispresented in a new context in a misleading way,(3) There is not enough evidence to verify the claim or the evidence is conflicting or self-contradictory.
* `not enough information`: The fact-check does not contain sufficient information to come to an conclusion. For example,there is substantial lack of evidence or the evidence is inconclusive, conflicting or self-contradictory. In the case of a lack of evidence, state which information exactly is missing. In particular, if no RESULTS or sources are available, pick this decision.
* `true`: The claim is factually accurate when it is confirmed by evidence from multiple and reliable sources.

## Valid Actions
* `reverse_search`
   * Description: Performs a reverse image search to find similar images on the web.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will perform a reverse search to find similar images.
   * Format: reverse_search(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `image_search`
   * Description: Run an image search on Google to retrieve related images for a given query.
   * How to use: This is a helpful tool for fact-checking images. Use this to retrieve images associated with a specific keyword or phrase. Ensure that the query is clear and specific to improve search accuracy. If no relevant images are found, refine the query or use more descriptive terms.
   * Format: image_search("your image search query goes here")

* `geolocate`
   * Description: Performs geolocation to determine the country where an image was taken.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will determine the most likely countries where it was taken.
   * Format: geolocate(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `web_search`
   * Description: Run an open web search on Google or DuckDuckGO to retrieve any related webpage.
   * How to use: Do not use this with a previously used or similar query from previous web searches. If a previous web search did not yield any results, use a very different query.
   * Format: web_search("your web search query goes here")

Ukraine Has Reportedly Lost About 40 Leopard Tanks Since February 2022
======================================================================

[10:12 17.10.2024](/20241017/ "News archive")
 (Updated: 13:02 17.10.2024)

© AP Photo / Michael SohnA Leopard 2 tank as a part of weapons deliveries to Ukraine

![A Leopard 2 tank as a part of weapons deliveries to Ukraine - Sputnik Africa, 1920, 17.10.2024](https://cdn1.img.sputniknews.africa/img/07e8/07/0d/1067487443_0:0:3564:2004_1920x0_80_0_0_7733207e8d6471ece40fd505c0b45362.jpg "A Leopard 2 tank as a part of weapons deliveries to Ukraine")

© AP Photo / Michael Sohn

Subscribe

MOSCOW (Sputnik) - Ukraine has lost around 40 Leopard tanks since the beginning of Russia's special military operation in February 2022, the Business Insider news outlet reported on Thursday.

Some open-source estimates suggest that Ukraine had already [lost](https://en.sputniknews.africa/20241013/1068665538.html)
 nearly 40 Leopards, but those estimates are unconfirmed so far, according to the report.

Russia repeatedly stated that arms supplies to Ukraine hinder the settlement and directly involve NATO countries in the conflict. Russian Foreign Minister Sergey Lavrov said that the United States and [NATO](https://en.sputniknews.africa/20240512/1066501213.html)
 were directly involved in the conflict not only by providing weapons but also by training Ukrainian personnel in European countries.

[![Leopard 2 and Bradley pictured among destroyed and damaged Ukrainian vehicles. Screenshot of Russian Defense Ministry video. - Sputnik Africa, 1920, 04.11.2023](https://cdn1.img.sputniknews.africa/img/07e7/08/05/1061086329_0:221:1360:765_1920x0_80_0_0_e3c9d50c9e4682697a50f5d445b1b805.jpg "Leopard 2 and Bradley pictured among destroyed and damaged Ukrainian vehicles. Screenshot of Russian Defense Ministry video.")](/20231104/quarter-of-leopard-2-tanks-written-off-by-ukraine-just-over-week-1063322121.html "Quarter of Leopard 2 Tanks 'Written Off' by Ukraine Just Over Week")

By [AFP](https://www.themoscowtimes.com/author/afp "AFP")

June 13, 2023

! <image:2769>

Ukrainian Armed Forces destroyed in the Zaporozhye direction. Russian Defence Ministry / TASS

Moscow said Tuesday that it had captured several German Leopard tanks and U.S. Bradley infantry fighting vehicles, releasing footage showing Russian troops surveying the equipment supplied to Ukraine by Western countries.

"Leopard tanks and Bradley infantry fighting vehicles. These are our trophies. Equipment of the Ukrainian armed forces in the Zaporizhzhia region," the Russian Defense Ministry said in a statement.

"Servicemen of the Vostok group inspect enemy tanks and infantry fighting vehicles captured in battle."

Kyiv has appealed to its allies in the West to deliver a broad range of modern military equipment to help Ukrainian forces recapture large swathes of territory controlled by Russian forces.

The Defense Ministry said several of the captured vehicles had working engines, suggesting that the battles they were involved in had been short and that Ukrainian troops had "fled" their offensive positions.

**(DEFENCE SECURITY ASIA) — During the week of May 11 to 17, Russian military claimed to have successfully destroyed five Leopard 2A1 tanks, manufactured by the German company Krauss-Maffei but donated to the Ukrainian Armed Forces to help the Eastern Europe country in its armed conflict with Russia.**

**In addition to the Leopard tanks, the Russian Ministry of Defense also alleged that 13 armored vehicles, 55 various vehicles, “Grad” multiple rocket launcher systems, and 47 artillery units—22 of which were supplied by foreign countries—were destroyed during this period.**

**Moreover, four Mi-24 helicopters and 40 unmanned boats belonging to the Ukrainian military were reportedly destroyed by Russia in the same timeframe.**

**Among the foreign-supplied armored vehicles to Ukraine, the Leopard tanks have been the most frequently supplied to Kyiv compared to other models such as the American-made Abrams and the British-made Challengers.**

**Since last year, countries such as Germany and several other European nations have supplied between 100-200 Leopard tanks to Ukraine for use in a spring counteroffensive against Russian positions.**

**“Russian Soldiers Pose in Front of Captured Leopard 2A6 Tank”**

**Line of Leopard tanks and Bradley armoured infantry fighting vehicle were destroyed in Zaphorizia, southern Ukraine.**

**Although the Ukrainian counteroffensive in 2023 initially started well, it faced increasingly formidable opposition from Russian forces who began altering their tactics and strategies.**

**These changes in strategy and tactics by the Russian forces led to the destruction of many of the Ukrainian tanks that had been supplied by donor countries like Germany, other European nations, the United States, and Britain.**

**However, to date, no one knows exactly how many Leopard tanks have been destroyed by Russia.**

**Nevertheless, Russian President Vladimir Putin has reportedly stated to his country’s war correspondents that Ukraine has lost more than 160 tanks supplied by foreign countries.**

**Given the high volume of Leopard tanks supplied to Ukraine, it is logical to conclude that many of the tanks destroyed by Russia were Leopard models.**

**Regarding the Abrams tanks, the Russian military stated that of the 31 American-made tanks supplied to Ukraine, more than five of the tanks have been destroyed by Russian forces.**

**A charred M1A1 Abrams main battle tank being transported to Moscow to participate in an exhibition at Victory Park.**

 **As a result of the destruction of five Abrams tanks, the United States has reportedly “withdrawn” these tanks from the Ukrainian battlefield, likely in an effort to “preserve its reputation.”**

**Following the destruction experienced by Leopard tanks supplied by Germany and other European countries, Ukraine’s Deputy Foreign Minister Andii Melnyk has requested that Kiev be supplied with more Leopard tanks, including the latest variant, the Leopard 2A6.**

 **However, the newest Leopard 2A6 variant supplied to Ukraine has met the same fate.**

**The Russian military reported capturing the most powerful tank in the Ukrainian arsenal, the German-made Leopard 2A6, after intense fighting in Avdiivka, Ukraine, last April.**

**It is believed that Ukraine possesses 21 Leopard 2A6 tanks, with 18 of these tanks developed by the companies Krauss-Maffei Wegmann and Rheinmetall being donated by Germany, while the remainder were provided by Portugal.**

**However, most of these Leopard 2A6 tanks donated to the Ukrainian military could not be used after failing to be properly maintained and remained inoperable as claimed by a senior German politician last January.**

**An Abrams tank caught fire after being struck by a Lancet kamikaze drone and an RPG from Russian forces.**

**According to Russian military sources, after capturing and removing the tank from the combat area, Russian forces transported the tank and sent it to Moscow, possibly for research purposes.**

**The Leopard 2A6 was successfully captured after a Russian platoon executed an ambush that caused the Ukrainian tank crew to abandon the German-made vehicle.**

**The Leopard 2A6 represents an upgrade from the Leopard 2A5, incorporating enhanced armor protection, firepower, and electronic warfare capabilities.**

**The tank measures 9.97 meters in length and weighs 62.3 tons, making it one of the heaviest main battle tanks ever deployed, with an engine power of 1,500 horsepower.**

**Capable of speeds up to 75 km/h and with an operational range of 500 km, it is equipped with a Rheinmetall 120 mm L/55 cannon, allowing it to fire all standard NATO ammunition types, including APFSDS, HEAT, and multi-purpose shells.**

**The Leopard 2A6 also features dual 7.62 mm MG3A1 machine guns and an advanced fire control system including a laser rangefinder, thermal imaging, and a ballistic computer. — DSA**

involvement in the Russian invasion of Ukraine")<br>    <br>*   [Azerbaijan Airlines Flight 8243](/wiki/Azerbaijan_Airlines_Flight_8243 "Azerbaijan Airlines Flight 8243")<br>    <br>*   _[Spider's Web](/wiki/Operation_Spider%27s_Web "Operation Spider's Web")<br>    _ |     |

On 6 August 2024, during the [Russian invasion of Ukraine](/wiki/Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine "Russian invasion of Ukraine")
,[\[36\]](#cite_note-dw.com-38)
[\[37\]](#cite_note-ft.com-39)
\[_[failed verification](/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability "Wikipedia:Verifiability")\
 – [see discussion](/wiki/Talk:Kursk_campaign#A_ridiculous_edit "Talk:Kursk campaign")\
_\] part of the [Russo-Ukrainian War](/wiki/Russo-Ukrainian_War "Russo-Ukrainian War")
, the [Armed Forces of Ukraine](/wiki/Armed_Forces_of_Ukraine "Armed Forces of Ukraine")
 launched an incursion into [Russia](/wiki/Russia "Russia")
's [Kursk Oblast](/wiki/Kursk_Oblast "Kursk Oblast")
 and clashed with the [Russian Armed Forces](/wiki/Russian_Armed_Forces "Russian Armed Forces")
 and [Russian border guard](/wiki/FSB_Border_Service_of_Russia "FSB Border Service of Russia")
.[\[38\]](#cite_note-REU86-40)
[\[36\]](#cite_note-dw.com-38)
[\[37\]](#cite_note-ft.com-39)
 A [state of emergency](/wiki/State_of_emergency_in_Russia "State of emergency in Russia")
 was declared in Kursk Oblast,[\[39\]](#cite_note-BBC_8_Aug-41)
 and Russian reserves were rushed to the area.[\[40\]](#cite_note-BBC_Cursino-42)
 By the end of the first week, the Ukrainian military said it had captured 1,000 km2 (390 sq mi) of Russian territory, while Russian authorities acknowledged that Ukraine had captured 28 settlements.[\[41\]](#cite_note-43)

In the second half of August the front stabilized,[\[42\]](#cite_note-forbes_20240911-44)
 and in early October, the Ukrainian advance had stalled.[\[11\]](#cite_note-CNN_Third_Month-12)
 From November, North Korean forces were sent to the province to support the Russian military. According to Russia, the incursion involved around 300 Ukrainian troops, 11 tanks, and over 20 [armored combat vehicles](/wiki/Armoured_fighting_vehicle "Armoured fighting vehicle")
,[\[67\]](#cite_note-MT86-69)
 and was aimed in two directions: at [Oleshnya](/wiki/Oleshnya,_Kursk_Oblast "Oleshnya, Kursk Oblast")
 in the direction of [Sudzha](/wiki/Sudzha "Sudzha")
, east-northeast of [Sumy](/wiki/Sumy "Sumy")
, and towards [Nikolayevo-Darino](/wiki/Nikolayevo-Darino "Nikolayevo-Darino")
, north-northeast of Sumy.[\[68\]](#cite_note-ISW_August_6-70)
 It was reported that Chechen [Akhmat battalions](/wiki/Russian_irregular_units_in_Ukraine#Akhmat_battalions "Russian irregular units in Ukraine")
 were responding to the raids,[\[68\]](#cite_note-ISW_August_6-70)
 though these claims remained unverified as of 13 September 2024.[\[69\]](#cite_note-71)

The attack began at 08:00 [MSK](/wiki/Moscow_Time "Moscow Time")
. [Alexei Smirnov](/wiki/Alexei_Smirnov_(politician) "Alexei Smirnov (politician)")
, acting [governor of Kursk Oblast](/wiki/Governor_of_Kursk_Oblast "Governor of Kursk Oblast")
, reported that three people died during the events: a woman in the border incursion and two individuals in separate drone attacks.[\[70\]](#cite_note-72)
 Russian [milbloggers](/wiki/Milblog "Milblog")
 also largely dismissed the supposed raids as "unsuccessful" and a "media stunt".[\[68\]](#cite_note-ISW_August_6-70)

According to Russia, at least 1,000 troops crossed the border on the first day, supported by [tanks](/wiki/Tank "Tank")
 and armored vehicles.[\[39\]](#cite_note-BBC_8_Aug-41)
 According to Andrzej Wilk of the [Centre for Eastern Studies](/wiki/Centre_for_Eastern_Studies "Centre for Eastern Studies")
, the entire Ukrainian grouping, including some elements which did not cross over into Russia, consisted of an estimated 2,000 men from Ukraine's [22nd](/wiki/22nd_Mechanized_Brigade_(Ukraine) "22nd Mechanized Brigade (Ukraine)")
 and [82nd](/wiki/82nd_Air_Assault_Brigade_(Ukraine) "82nd Air Assault Brigade (Ukraine)")
 Brigades, supported by artillery and air defense sub-units.[\[66\]](#cite_note-wilk-68)
 It was later claimed by members of the Ukrainian military that the breakthrough on the border was conducted by the 80th and 82nd Air Assault Brigades.[\[64\]](#cite_note-Kyrylenko-66)

Russian milbloggers claimed that the offensive was being performed by the [Russian Volunteer Corps](/wiki/Russian_Volunteer_Corps "Russian Volunteer Corps")
 (RVC), while the _[New Voice of Ukraine](/wiki/New_Voice_of_Ukraine "New Voice of Ukraine")
_ citing a source in [Ukraine's Main Military Intelligence](/wiki/Ukraine%27s_Main_Military_Intelligence "Ukraine's Main Military Intelligence")
 reported that the RVC was not present.[\[68\]](#cite_note-ISW_August_6-70)

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B6%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D0%B4%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%BF%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%92%D0%A1%D0%A3_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%9A%D1%83%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BA%D1%83%D1%8E_%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%BB%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C.jpg/250px-%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B6%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D0%B4%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%BF%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%92%D0%A1%D0%A3_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%9A%D1%83%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BA%D1%83%D1%8E_%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%BB%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C.jpg)](/wiki/File:%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B6%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D0%B4%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%BF%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%92%D0%A1%D0%A3_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%9A%D1%83%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BA%D1%83%D1%8E_%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%BB%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C.jpg)

Building damaged in Kursk Oblast, 6 August 2024

#### 7 August

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Ukrainian_%22Southern_Railway%22_1943.jpg/250px-Ukrainian_%22Southern_Railway%22_1943.jpg)](/wiki/File:Ukrainian_%22Southern_Railway%22_1943.jpg)

1943 Ukrainian railway map shows Sudzha in quadrant A2 at km 60 on the [Lgov](/wiki/Lgov,_Kursk_Oblast "Lgov, Kursk Oblast")
–[Gotnya](/wiki/Gotnya "Gotnya")
–[Zolochiv](/wiki/Zolochiv,_Kharkiv_Oblast "Zolochiv, Kharkiv Oblast")
 main line to [Kharkiv](/wiki/Kharkiv "Kharkiv")

A milblogger claimed that Ukrainian forces had captured 11 settlements and had advanced 14 kilometres (9 mi) deep into the oblast.[\[71\]](#cite_note-NBC87-73)
 Government agencies were ordered by President [Vladimir Putin](/wiki/Vladimir_Putin "Vladimir Putin")
 to "provide the needed assistance to residents", and deputy prime minister [Denis Manturov](/wiki/Denis_Manturov "Denis Manturov")
 was sent to oversee their work.[\[72\]](#cite_note-mt1-74)
 Kursk Oblast was placed under a [state of emergency](/wiki/State_of_emergency "State of emergency")
 by governor Smirnov.[\[73\]](#cite_note-dw1-75)
[\[74\]](#cite_note-CNBC_State_of_Emergency-76)

Putin met with key members of the security establishment including [Valery Gerasimov](/wiki/Valery_Gerasimov "Valery Gerasimov")
, [Alexander Bortnikov](/wiki/Alexander_Bortnikov "Alexander Bortnikov")
, [Sergei Shoigu](/wiki/Sergei_Shoigu "Sergei Shoigu")
 and [Andrey Belousov](/wiki/Andrey_Belousov "Andrey Belousov")
 on the Kursk incursion.[\[75\]](#cite_note-kru1-77)
 Gerasimov told Putin that about 1,000 Ukrainian soldiers took part in the attack and that their advance had been halted.[\[74\]](#cite_note-CNBC_State_of_Emergency-76)
[\[76\]](#cite_note-Reuters_Videos_show_Ukrainian_Presence-78)

Geolocated footage confirmed that Ukrainian forces had advanced at least 10 kilometres (6.2 mi) across the Russian border, having penetrated at least two Russian defensive lines and a stronghold. Russian officials said that the loss of the bridge would hinder the relocation via land routes of civilians in the district.[\[151\]](#cite_note-153)
[\[152\]](#cite_note-154)
 Approximately 2,000 to 3,000 Russian conscripts were trapped in a [pocket](/wiki/Pocket_(military) "Pocket (military)")
 south of the river.[\[153\]](#cite_note-155)

#### 17 August

Russian forces reportedly blew up two bridges near [Tyotkino](/wiki/Tyotkino "Tyotkino")
 and [Popovo-Lezhachi](/wiki/Popovo-Lezhachi "Popovo-Lezhachi")
 after withdrawing from the right bank of the [Seym River](/wiki/Seym_River "Seym River")
 in the area.[\[154\]](#cite_note-156)

The Ukrainian military claimed the capture of the settlement of [Korenevo](/wiki/Korenevo,_Korenevsky_District,_Kursk_Oblast "Korenevo, Korenevsky District, Kursk Oblast")
 but the Russian MOD described the settlement as contested.[\[155\]](#cite_note-157)

#### 18 August

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/The_80th_Air_Assault_Brigade_captured_a_T-90M_Proryv_tank_in_the_Kursk_region.jpg/250px-The_80th_Air_Assault_Brigade_captured_a_T-90M_Proryv_tank_in_the_Kursk_region.jpg)](/wiki/File:The_80th_Air_Assault_Brigade_captured_a_T-90M_Proryv_tank_in_the_Kursk_region.jpg)

Ukrainian soldiers with a captured Russian [T-90](/wiki/T-90 "T-90")
M Proryv tank

Ukrainian forces destroyed another bridge over the [Seym](/wiki/Seym_(river) "Seym (river)")
 river near [Zvannoye](/wiki/Zvannoye "Zvannoye")
.[\[156\]](#cite_note-158)
[\[157\]](#cite_note-ISW_2024-08-16-159)
[\[158\]](#cite_note-160)

According to Russian bloggers, both Ukraine and Russia reinforced their forces battling in Kursk Oblast, with Russia moving some forces from other fronts to the front.[\[159\]](#cite_note-newsweek20240818-161)
\[_[better source needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS "Wikipedia:NOTRS")\
_\]

Marines from the [501st Separate Naval Infantry Battalion](/wiki/501st_Separate_Naval_Infantry_Battalion "501st Separate Naval Infantry Battalion")
 posted a video of them tearing down the Russian flag from the municipal building of [Apanasovka](/wiki/Apanasovka,_Korenevsky_District,_Kursk_Oblast "Apanasovka, Korenevsky District, Kursk Oblast")
.[\[160\]](#cite_note-162)

#### 19 August

Russia claimed that the Ukrainian military destroyed the third and last bridge over the Seym River in [Korenevsky District](/wiki/Korenevsky_District "Korenevsky District")
 leading to possible logistical strain on over 700 square kilometers of Russian territory.[\[161\]](#cite_note-163)

In his evening address, President Zelenskyy said that Ukrainian forces were in control of 92 settlements in Kursk Oblast and 1,250 square kilometers of Russian territory.[\[162\]](#cite_note-164)

#### 20 August

The Russian interior ministry warned residents of Bryansk, Kursk and Belgorod Oblasts against using online dating websites and security cameras, citing concerns of information being gathered by Ukrainian forces.[\[163\]](#cite_note-165)
 [Yunus-Bek Yevkurov](/wiki/Yunus-Bek_Yevkurov "Yunus-Bek Yevkurov")
, former head of [Ingushetia](/wiki/Ingushetia "Ingushetia")
 and incumbent deputy head of the Ministry of Defense was appointed as [Andrei Belousov](/wiki/Andrei_Belousov "Andrei Belousov")
's deputy in the Coordinating Council for the Security Issues of the Bordering Territories. Some officials hoped it could be the first step toward a more comprehensive peace deal.[\[306\]](#cite_note-washingtonpost-qatar-308)
 Russian foreign ministry spokesperson [Maria Zakharova](/wiki/Maria_Zakharova "Maria Zakharova")
 said that there were "no direct or indirect negotiations between Russia and Ukraine on the safety of civilian critical infrastructure facilities" and that after the assault on Kursk Oblast, Putin ruled out the possibility of such talks.[\[396\]](#cite_note-euractiv-qatar-398)
[\[397\]](#cite_note-399)
 A Russian academic with close ties to senior Russian diplomats said that Putin probably lost interest in further talks in Qatar because the "Russian leadership usually does not make any compromises under pressure" and attacks on energy infrastructure are highly effective tactics that do more damage to Ukraine than to Russia, adding that Russia is more interested in talks with Ukraine about a broader ceasefire.[\[306\]](#cite_note-washingtonpost-qatar-308)

The level of anxiety among Russians was much less than that after the [2022 mobilization](/wiki/2022_Russian_mobilization "2022 Russian mobilization")
, according to a [Levada](/wiki/Levada_Center "Levada Center")
 poll.[\[389\]](#cite_note-Sort-391)
[\[398\]](#cite_note-Levada2024-400)

The incursion led the [Russian Central Election Commission](/wiki/Central_Election_Commission_(Russia) "Central Election Commission (Russia)")
 to postpone voting for the [2024 Russian elections](/wiki/2024_Russian_elections "2024 Russian elections")
 in seven municipalities located in occupied areas of Kursk Oblast that were originally scheduled for 6–8 September.[\[399\]](#cite_note-401)
 In Belgorod Oblast, authorities ordered the start of classes in September to be held online in areas within 20 kilometers of the Ukrainian border.[\[400\]](#cite_note-402)

According to BBC journalists, Russian soldiers in territories of Kursk Oblast near the front engaged in [looting](/wiki/Looting "Looting")
.[\[401\]](#cite_note-403)

Casualties
----------

### Russia

Ukraine claimed their forces had shot down an [Mi-28](/wiki/Mil_Mi-28 "Mil Mi-28")
 and two [Ka-52](/wiki/Ka-52 "Ka-52")
[\[23\]](#cite_note-KI86-24)
[\[24\]](#cite_note-Ka52-2-25)
 helicopters.[\[402\]](#cite_note-Mi28-404)

On 9 August 2024, [HIMARS](/wiki/M142_HIMARS "M142 HIMARS")
 destroyed a convoy of Russian troops in Kursk Oblast in what Russian milbloggers described as one of the bloodiest attacks of the entire war.[\[95\]](#cite_note-telegraph-column-97)
[\[403\]](#cite_note-405)

On 12 August, Ukrainian military expert Mykhailo Zhirokhov claimed that the ratio of Ukrainian to Russian manpower losses as "closer to 1 to 10", and the number of Russian POWs taken as "thousands".[\[404\]](#cite_note-406)
 Since most of the best Russian troops were deployed in Ukraine, most of the Russian soldiers protecting the Russian border in the Kursk region were young, inexperienced [conscripts](/wiki/Conscription_in_Russia "Conscription in Russia")
 who suffered heavy losses in combat with experienced Ukrainian troops.[\[390\]](#cite_note-thebarentsobserver-392)
[\[59\]](#cite_note-cnn-conscripts-61)

On 19 August, the Ukrainian resistance group [Atesh](/wiki/Atesh "Atesh")
 claimed that a battalion from the [810th Guards Naval Infantry Brigade](/wiki/810th_Guards_Naval_Infantry_Brigade "810th Guards Naval Infantry Brigade")
 had suffered heavy losses and had only 30% of its combat personnel left.[\[405\]](#cite_note-407)
 According to a Western official, about 1,000 Russian soldiers were killed or wounded daily in the fighting in Kursk and Donbas.[\[406\]](#cite_note-408)

As of 23 September 2024, Russian officials reported that at least 56 civilians had been killed since the start of the incursion, while at least 266 others, including 11 children, had been injured.[\[407\]](#cite_note-56dead-409)
 The Russian state broadcaster [Russia-24](/wiki/Russia-24 "Russia-24")
 announced that one of its reporters, [Evgeniy Poddubny](/wiki/Evgeniy_Poddubny "Evgeniy Poddubny")
, had been injured in a drone attack on his vehicle while reporting on the fighting in the affected areas on 7 August.[\[408\]](#cite_note-410)
 On 16 August, the [All-Russia People's Front](/wiki/All-Russia_People%27s_Front "All-Russia People's Front")
 said that one of its medical staff and a media coordinator had been killed after their vehicle was shelled while assisting in evacuation efforts.[\[409\]](#cite_note-411)
 At least 770 residents of Kursk Oblast went missing following the incursion.[\[407\]](#cite_note-56dead-409)
 Around 20,000 civilians are believed to be living under Ukrainian occupation in the oblast.[\[410\]](#cite_note-412)
 In October 2024, Russian human rights commissioner [Tatyana Moskalkova](/wiki/Tatyana_Moskalkova "Tatyana Moskalkova")
 accused Ukraine of forcibly taking more than 1,000 residents of Kursk Oblast.[\[411\]](#cite_note-413)

On 25 October 2024, Ukrainian Commander-in-Chief Colonel-General [Oleksandr Syrskyi](/wiki/Oleksandr_Syrskyi "Oleksandr Syrskyi")
 claimed Russian soldiers had suffered 17,819 casualties since 8 August 2024, of which 6,662 had been killed, 10,446 wounded and 711 captured.[\[412\]](#cite_note-414)

On 10 November, the Ukrainian 95th Airborne Assault Brigade claimed to have repelled an assault by the Russian [810th Marine Brigade](/wiki/810th_Naval_Infantry_Brigade "810th Naval Infantry Brigade")
, killing 100 and wounding 100 personnel in two days, while also destroying 28 pieces of equipment.[\[413\]](#cite_note-c010-415)

On 20 November, the Ukrainian [80th Air Assault Brigade](/wiki/80th_Air_Assault_Brigade_(Ukraine) "80th Air Assault Brigade (Ukraine)")
 claimed to have captured 26 Russian soldiers in a single battle on Kursk Oblast.[\[414\]](#cite_note-h833-416)

On 27 December, the South Korean [National Intelligence Service](/wiki/National_Intelligence_Service_(South_Korea) "National Intelligence Service (South Korea)")
 said that a North Korean soldier had been taken prisoner by Ukrainian forces for the first time in Kursk Oblast. Khinstein said that the bodies of killed civilians in the region were being recovered, but gave no details on how they had died.[\[32\]](#cite_note-mt288-34)

### Ukraine

Russia claimed that six Ukrainian tanks and ten armored vehicles were lost in the initial engagement on 6 August.[\[67\]](#cite_note-MT86-69)
[\[425\]](#cite_note-Novaya-427)
[\[426\]](#cite_note-UkrRetreat2-428)
 Acting governor of Kursk Oblast, [Alexei Smirnov](/wiki/Alexei_Smirnov_(politician) "Alexei Smirnov (politician)")
, claimed that 26 Ukrainian UAVs were shot down in the area.[\[427\]](#cite_note-nocomment-429)
 Russia later claimed on 9 August, that Ukraine had losses of 945 soldiers and 102 armored vehicles, although this could not be verified.[\[76\]](#cite_note-Reuters_Videos_show_Ukrainian_Presence-78)

On 17 August, Forbes reported "heavy Ukrainian equipment write-offs compared to relatively few Russian write-offs."[\[428\]](#cite_note-430)

[DeepStateMap.Live](/wiki/DeepStateMap.Live "DeepStateMap.Live")
 reported that nine Ukrainian "drone operators and contractors" were shot after surrendering to Russian forces on 10 October.[\[429\]](#cite_note-431)

As of 7 August 2025, UALosses listed Ukrainian casualties during the Kursk campaign as 2,588 dead, 9,622 missing and 306 captured Ukrainian soldiers.[\[430\]](#cite_note-432)

#### 8 August

[RIA Novosti](/wiki/RIA_Novosti "RIA Novosti")
 reported that four people died as a result of 'attacks' by the [AFU](/wiki/Armed_Forces_of_Ukraine "Armed Forces of Ukraine")
 in the oblast[\[81\]](#cite_note-Rai_2024-08-08-2-83)
 as fighting continued for the third day.[\[82\]](#cite_note-Reuters_2024-08-08-84)
[\[83\]](#cite_note-AlJazeera_2024-08-08-85)

.[\[84\]](#cite_note-86)

Ukrainian forces were in control of the western part of Sudzha and the surrounding roads; skirmishes continued in the town.[\[85\]](#cite_note-agent-87)

According to Smirnov, the acting governor of Kursk Oblast, six Ukrainian drones and five missiles were shot down during the night and morning.[\[86\]](#cite_note-meduzalive8aug-88)
